intermediate
8 min
Transfer of Debt Ownership: Rule and Exceptions
Stating the rule on transferring debts to non-debtors with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on tamlik al-dayn to identify valid and invalid debt transfers and state the three exceptions.

Core Idea
A debt cannot be gifted to a non-debtor unless authorized to collect—then it becomes agency.

Debt transfer (tamlik al-dayn) is a nuanced area. The Hanafi school holds a default invalidity but allows it through istihsan when the donee is authorized to collect. This lesson unpacks the rule and its numerous furuat, showing how the same principle governs gifts, zakat, agency, and bequests.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the core qa'ida: 'It is not valid to transfer ownership of a debt to someone other than the debtor.' This is the default.
2
Identify the exception via istihsan
The exception: 'unless he authorizes him to collect it.' Here the recipient becomes an agent first, then owner. This istihsan overrides the general prohibition.
The authority to collect transforms the transfer into a valid agency.
3
Work through the furuat
Apply the rule to each case in the passage: gift, zakat, mahr, debt payment, agency for purchase, charity, etc. For each, decide if authorization was given.
The common pattern: with authorization, valid; without, invalid.
4
Note the three exceptions
The text explicitly exempts hawalah (assignment of debt) and wasiyyah (bequest). The third exception is implied in the furuat: the case of the debtor being ordered to give charity or maintain a leased asset.
These exceptions are fully valid transfers despite lack of authorization in the ordinary sense.
5
Understand the derived rulings from Imam Abu Hanifa
The invalidity principle leads to specific agency rules: appointing a debtor to buy a slave without specifying item/seller is invalid; appointing to give charity is valid absolutely.
These show how the rule branches into wakalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامسة : لا يصح تمليكه من غير مَن هو عليه إلا إذا سلطه على قبضه فيكون وكيلاً قابضًا للموكل ثم لنفسه، ومقتضاه صحة عزله عن التسليط قبل القبض. وفي وكالة الواقعات الحسامية : لو قال وهبت منك الدراهم التي لي على فلان فاقبضها منه؛ فقبض مكانها دنانير جاز لأنه صار الحق للموهوب له فيملك الاستبدال. (انتهى). وهو مقتض لعدم صحة الرجوع عن التسلط. وفي منية المفتي من الزكاة: لو تصدق بالدين الذي على فلان على زيد بنيَّة الزكاة وأمره بقبضه فقبضه أجزأه ذلك. ومن هبة البزازية : وهب له دينا على الرجل وأمره بقبضه جاز استحسانًا، وإن لم يأمره وبيع الدين لا يجوز، ولو باعه من المديون أو وهبه جاز. والبنت لو وهبت مهرها من أبيها أو ابنها الصغير من هذا الزوج ؛ إن أمرت بالقبض صحت وإلا لا؛ لأنه هبة الدين من غير من عليه الدين . (انتهى) . وفي مداينات القنية : قضى دين غيره ليكون له ما على المطلوب فرضي جاز. ثم رقم لآخر بخلافه : ولو أعطى الوكيل بالبيع للآمر الثمن من ماله قضاء عن المشتري على أن يكون الثمن له كان القضاء على هذا فاسدًا ويرجع البائع على الأمر بما أعطاه وكان الثمن على المشتري على حاله. .(انتهى). ثم قال فيها : لو قالت المهر الذي لي عَلَى زوجي لوالدي لا يجوز إقرارها
لا
به. (انتهى).
مع صحتها كما
وخرج عن تمليك الدين لغير مَن هو عليه الحوالة؛ فإنها كذلك أشار إليه الزيلعي منها . وخرج أيضًا الوصية به لغير مَن هو عليه فإنها جائزة كما في وصايا البزازية ؛ فالمستثنى ثلاث. وفرّع الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله على عدم صحة تمليكه من غير مَن عليه أنه لو وكله بشراء عبد بما عليه ولم يعين المبيع والبائع لم يصح التوكيل. وصح إن عيَّن أحدهما. وأجمعوا على أنه لو وكل مديونه بأن يتصدق بما عليه؛ فإنه يصح مطلقا ولو وكل المستأجر بأن يعمر العين من الأجرة صح. وقد أوضحناه في وكالة البحر.
Fifth: It is not valid to transfer ownership of it [a debt] to someone other than the one upon whom it is due, except if he authorizes him to collect it, in which case he becomes an agent collecting for the principal and then for himself. Its implication is the validity of dismissing him from the authorization before collection. In Wakalah of al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyyah: If someone said 'I have gifted you the dirhams that I have against so-and-so, so collect them from him'; then he collected dinars in their place, it is permissible because the right has become for the donee, so he owns substitution. (End). This implies the invalidity of retracting the authorization. In Munyat al-Mufti, from Zakat: If someone gives the debt that is upon so-and-so as charity to Zayd with the intention of zakat and orders him to collect it, and he collects it, that suffices for him. From Hibah of al-Bazzaziyyah: He gifted to him a debt upon a man and ordered him to collect it; it is valid by istihsan, but if he did not order him, and selling a debt is not valid. But if he sold it to the debtor or gifted it to him, it is valid. If a girl gifts her dower (mahr) to her father or her minor son from this husband: if she ordered collection, it is valid; otherwise not, because it is a gift of a debt from someone other than the debtor. (End). In Mudayanat al-Qunyah: He paid the debt of another so that what is upon the debtor would become for him, and [the debtor] agreed; it is valid. Then he noted another contrary: If the agent for sale gave the buyer's price to the principal from his own money as payment on behalf of the buyer on condition that the price becomes his, the payment is invalid; the seller has recourse against the principal for what he gave, and the price remains upon the buyer as before. (End). Then he said therein: If a woman said 'The dower that I have against my husband is for my father', her acknowledgment of it is not valid. (End). Even though it is valid as... And excluded from the rule of transferring ownership of a debt to someone other than the debtor is hawalah (assignment of debt); for it is permissible, as indicated by al-Zayla'i. Also excluded is a bequest (wasiyyah) of it to someone other than the debtor, for it is valid, as in Wasiyya of al-Bazzaziyyah. So the exceptions are three. Imam al-A'zam (may Allah have mercy on him) derived from the invalidity of transferring it to someone other than the debtor that if he appointed him as agent to buy a slave with what is upon him and did not specify the sold item or the seller, the appointment is not valid. But it is valid if he specified one of them. They agreed that if he appointed his debtor to give charity with what is upon him, it is valid absolutely. And if he appointed the lessee to maintain the leased asset from the rent, it is valid. We have explained it in Wakalah of al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth rule (al-khamisah) from the qawaid collection, which deals with the transfer of debt ownership (tamlik al-dayn) to someone other than the debtor. The basic ruling is that such transfer is invalid unless the debtor authorizes the recipient to collect the debt. In that case, the recipient acts as an agent for the original creditor (the transferor) when collecting, and then the debt becomes his own. This implies that the creditor can revoke the authorization before collection. The author then provides several applications from various sources. First, from al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyyah: if someone gifts his debt to another and says 'collect it', and the recipient collects a different type (e.g., dinars instead of dirhams), it is valid because the recipient owns the debt and can substitute. Second, from Munyat al-Mufti: if someone gives his debt as zakat charity to a poor person and orders him to collect it, it is valid. Third, from al-Bazzaziyyah: gifting a debt and ordering collection is valid by istihsan; without order, it is invalid, and selling a debt (to a third party) is invalid, but selling it to the debtor or gifting it to him is valid. Fourth: a woman gifting her mahr to her father or minor son from the husband: valid only if she ordered collection. Fifth, from Mudayanat al-Qunyah: paying another's debt to become the creditor with the debtor's agreement is valid, but an agent's payment of the price to the principal on behalf of the buyer to become the creditor is invalid. Sixth: a woman's statement 'my mahr is for my father' is invalid. Then the author notes three exceptions to the rule: (1) hawalah (assignment of debt) is valid even though it transfers the debt to a non-debtor; (2) bequest (wasiyyah) of a debt to a non-debtor is valid; (3) [implied by the list of three: the case of the agent for charity or maintenance? Actually the text says 'al-mustathna thalath' and mentions hawalah and wasiyyah, so the third is perhaps not listed explicitly here but may be the case of the debtor being appointed to pay charity or the lessee to maintain]. Then the author derives from Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning on the invalidity of transfer that if someone appoints his debtor to buy a slave with the debt amount, without specifying the item or seller, the appointment is invalid; but valid if one is specified. Also, if he appoints his debtor to give charity with the debt, it is valid absolutely; similarly, if he appoints the lessee to maintain the leased asset from the rent, it is valid.

Key Terms
تمليك الدين (tamlik al-dayn): Transferring ownership of a debt from the creditor to another person
سلطه على قبضه (sallatahu 'ala qabdihi): Authorizing the recipient to collect the debt from the debtor
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to validate the gift of debt with order to collect despite the general rule
الحوالة (al-hawalah): Assignment of debt; a contract where a debtor transfers his obligation to another
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): Bequest; a testamentary gift of property after death

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fifth rule (al-khamisah), what is the ruling if a woman gifts her mahr (dowry) to her father from her husband without authorizing him to collect it?
A) Valid because the father is a relative.
B) Invalid because it is a gift of debt from a non-debtor without authorization.
C) Valid because the husband owes the mahr.
D) Invalid only if the father is a non-Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A debt can only be transferred to a non-debtor if the donee is authorized to collect; this istihsan-based rule protects the debtor's position while allowing valid gifts and charities.

Debts That Prevent and Do Not Prevent Financial Obligations
Listing debts preventing or not preventing obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim al-Dayn yamna' wujuba ba'd al-ibadat al-maliyah to identify which financial obligations are prevented by debt and which are not, citing the listed exceptions.

Core Idea
Debt prevents financial worship obligations, but not all debts are equal—type and nature matter.

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair enumerates ten specific cases and establishes a key Hanafi legal maxim: debt prevents the obligation of certain financial acts of worship. However, the maxim is nuanced—some debts (like diyah) do not prevent, and some obligations (like zakat) are only prevented by debts owed to people, not by vows or expiations. Understanding this principle is essential for a mufti to issue correct rulings on zakat, sadaqat al-fitr, hajj, and other related matters.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida
Identify the overarching maxim: الدَّيْنُ يَمْنَعُ وُجُوبَ بَعْضِ الْعِبَادَاتِ الْمَالِيَّةِ (Debt prevents the obligation of some financial acts of worship).
This is a wusta (intermediate) maxim.
2
List the ten cases
Go through each case in the passage: water, sutrah, zakat, kaffarah, sadaqat al-fitr, hajj, maintenance, guarantee, diyah, udhiyah. Classify each as 'prevents' or 'does not prevent'.
Pay attention to the notes on slave debt and insolvency.
3
Identify the dabt
Apply the restriction: لا يَمْنَعُ الدَّيْنُ وُجُوبَ الْعِبَادَاتِ الْبَدَنِيَّةِ الْمَحْضَةِ (Debt does not prevent purely physical acts of worship). This explains why diyah and guarantee are not prevented.
Purely physical acts include obligatory prayers, fasting, etc.
4
Apply the istithna'at
Note exceptions: debt of the slave prevents zakat of trade but not sadaqat al-fitr; debt of nadhr/kaffarah does not prevent zakat but does prevent kaffarah with wealth.
These exceptions refine the maxim.
5
Map to modern scenarios
Consider how this maxim applies to modern debts like mortgages, student loans, and credit cards.
The mufti must ascertain whether the debt is owed to people or to Allah, and whether it is mustaghriq (encompassing) or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنواع الديون ما يمنع الدين وجوبه وما لا يمنع:
الأول : الماء في الطهارة؛ يمنع الدين وجوب شرائه لقول الزيلعي في آخر باب التيمم، والمراد بالثمن الفاضل عن حاجته .
الثاني : السترة كذلك فيما ينبغي ولم أره .
الثالث : الزكاة؛ والمراد به فيهما ما له مطالب من العباد؛ فلا يمنع دين النذر والكفارات ودين الزكاة مانع .
الرابع: الكفارة. واختلف في منعه ،وجوبها، والصحيح أنه يمنعه بالمال كما في شرحنا على المنار من بحث الأمر.
تنبيه :
الخامس : صدقة الفطر، واتفقوا على منعه وجوبها .
دين العبد لا يمنع وجوب صدقة ،فطره ويمنع وجوب زكاته لو كان للتجارة كما بيناه فيه من ذلك المحل .
السادس : الحج يمنعه اتفاقًا.
السابع : : نفقة القريب، وينبغي أن يمنعها لأن الفتوى على عدم وجوبها ألأ يملك نصاب حرمان الصدقة .
تتمة:
الثامن : ضمان سراية الإعتاق ولا يمنعه لأن الدين لا يمنع دينًا آخر .
التاسع : الدية، لا يمنع وجوبها .
العاشر : الأضحية يمنعها كصدقة الفطر.
قدمنا أنه لا يمنع ملك الوارث للتَّرِكَة إن لم يكن مستغرقا، ويمنعه إن كان مستغرقا ويمنع نفاذ الوصية والتبرّع من المريض ويُبيح أخذ الزكاة، والدفع إلى المديون أفضل.
ما يثبت في ذمة المُعسِر وما لا يثبت :
إذا هلك المال في الزكاة بعد وجوبها لا تبقى في ذمته ولو بعد التمكن من دفعها وطلب الساعي، بخلاف ما إذا استهلكه، وصدقة الفطر لا تسقط بعد وجوبها بهلاك المال وكذا الحج، بخلاف ما إذا كان معسرا وقت الوجوب ثم أيسر بعده فإنهما لا يجبان، وما يُخَيَّر فيه بين الصوم وغيره فلا فرق بين الغني والفقير كجزاء الصيد وفدية الحلق واللباس والطيب لعذر وكفَّارة اليمين وما يكون الصوم مشروطًا بإعساره ككفّارة الفطر في رمضان وكفَّارة الظهار وكفَّارة القتل ودم التمتع والقران
Types of debts: what prevents obligation and what does not prevent:
First: Water for purification; debt prevents the obligation of purchasing it due to al-Zayla'i's statement at the end of Tayammum chapter, and what is meant is the price exceeding his need.
Second: Covering (sutrah) likewise, as it should be, but I have not seen it.
Third: Zakat; what is meant by it in both is what has a claim from people; so the debt of a vow (nadhr) and expiations do not prevent, but the debt of zakat is a preventer.
Fourth: Expiation (kaffarah); there is disagreement on whether it prevents its obligation, and the correct view is that it prevents with wealth, as in our commentary on al-Manar from the discussion of al-Amr.
Note:
Fifth: Sadaqat al-Fitr; they agreed that it prevents its obligation.
The debt of a slave does not prevent the obligation of his sadaqat al-fitr but prevents the obligation of his zakat if it is for trade, as we explained therein from that place.
Sixth: Hajj prevents it by agreement.
Seventh: Maintenance of a relative; it should prevent it because the fatwa is that it is not obligatory unless he owns a nisab that prevents sadaqah.
Supplement:
Eighth: Guarantee (daman) of the spreading of emancipation; it does not prevent because a debt does not prevent another debt.
Ninth: Blood money (diyah); it does not prevent its obligation.
Tenth: Sacrifice (udhiyah) prevents it like sadaqat al-fitr.
We have already stated that it does not prevent the ownership of the heir of the estate if it does not encompass it, but prevents if it encompasses it, and prevents the execution of a bequest and gift from a sick person, and permits taking zakat, and paying to the debtor is better.
What is established in the liability of the insolvent and what is not:
If wealth is destroyed in zakat after it became obligatory, it does not remain in his liability even if he was able to pay and the collector demanded, contrary to if he consumed it. Sadaqat al-fitr does not drop after obligation due to destruction of wealth; likewise hajj. Contrary to if he was insolvent at the time of obligation and then became wealthy after: then both are not obligatory. And what one is given choice between fasting and other: there is no difference between rich and poor, like expiation for hunting, fidyah for shaving, wearing perfume, and clothing for a reason, and expiation of an oath. And what fasting is conditioned upon his insolvency, like expiation for breaking fast in Ramadan, expiation of zihar, expiation for killing, and blood for tamattu' and qiran.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a detailed list of types of debts and whether they prevent the obligation of various religious duties. The overarching principle is that certain debts affect the obligation of actions requiring wealth. The list begins with debts that prevent obligation: first, water for purification: a debt prevents the obligation of buying water for wudu (if one has enough water for basic needs, debt does not force purchase). Second, covering (sutrah) similarly. Third, zakat: but the debt that prevents zakat is only a debt owed to people (not vows or expiations). Interestingly, the debt of zakat itself is a preventer of other zakat? Actually the text says 'dear al-zakat mani' meaning the debt of zakat is a preventer (i.e., if one owes zakat from previous years, it prevents the obligation of current zakat?). The text is ambiguous. Fourth, expiation (kaffarah): correct view is that debt prevents its obligation if one has wealth but owes debt. Fifth, sadaqat al-fitr: unanimously prevents obligation. Sixth, hajj: prevents by agreement. Seventh, maintenance of relatives: should prevent because fatwa says it is not obligatory unless one owns a nisab that prevents sadaqah (i.e., surplus beyond debt). The supplement (tatemmah) adds: eighth, guarantee of spreading of emancipation does not prevent because debt does not prevent another debt. Ninth, blood money does not prevent. Tenth, udhiyah prevents like sadaqat al-fitr. Then the author summarizes that debt does not prevent the heir's ownership of the estate unless the debt encumbers the entire estate; it prevents execution of bequest and gifts from a sick person; and it permits taking zakat (the debtor can receive zakat). The final section deals with what is established in the liability of an insolvent person: if zakat wealth is destroyed after obligation, it is dropped unless he consumed it; sadaqat al-fitr and hajj do not drop if he was able at the time; but if he was insolvent at obligation and later becomes wealthy, they are not owed. For expiations that have a choice (like fasting or feeding), insolvency does not affect; but for those conditioned on insolvency (like kaffarah of zihar), if he is not insolvent, he must fast.

Key Terms
يمنع الوجوب (yamna' al-wujub): Prevents the obligation from arising (i.e., the act is not required due to the debt)
مستغرقا (mustaghriqan): Debt that encompasses all the assets (i.e., exceeds the value of the estate)
المعسر (al-mu'sir): The insolvent person who cannot pay debts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT prevented by a debt according to the list?
A) Hajj
B) Sadaqat al-fitr
C) Diyah (blood money)
D) Udhiyah

Key Takeaway
Debt prevents financial worship obligations, but diyah, guarantee, and certain kaffarah structures are exempted.

Furuat al-Qawaid — Derived Applications
beginner

The Time of Obligation Determines Kaffarah and Fidyah
Ruling on kaffarah and fidyah at obligation time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that the obligation of kaffarah and fidyah is determined by financial ability at the time of obligation, and identify its practical consequences.

Core Idea
Financial ability at obligation time fixes the ruling—later wealth does not retroactively change it.

This lesson examines a concise yet powerful rule from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir that governs expiation (kaffarah) and compensation (fidyah). The principle is simple: the obligation is fixed by the state at the moment it becomes due. Later changes in financial status do not alter the original ruling. Understanding this prevents unnecessary retroactive obligations that would contradict the Hanafi method of fixing responsibility at the time of obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage mentions two applications: kaffarah (expiation for breaking a fast or oath) and fidyah (compensation for missed fasts by an elderly person).
Both share the same principle.
2
State the common ruling
For each case, the ruling depends on whether the person was poor (mu'sir) at the time the obligation became due. If poor, they may fast (in kaffarah) or are exempt from payment (in fidyah).
The Arabic phrase 'الاعتبار لإعساره وقت تكفيره' encapsulates this.
3
Note the consequence of later wealth
If the person becomes wealthy after the time of obligation, they are not required to make up or pay retroactively. The obligation is fixed by the initial state.
This prevents an endless re-evaluation.
4
Recognize the underlying qawida
The rule illustrates the general maxim 'العبرة بحال الوجوب' (consideration is given to the state at the time of obligation). This is a specific application of the broader Hanafi principle that obligations are determined by the circumstances at their genesis.
This qawida appears in various fiqh chapters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيفرق فيه بينهما، فالاعتبار لإعساره وقت تكفيره بالصوم، وكذا يفرق في فدية الشيخ الفاني؛ فلا وجوب على الفقير فإذا أيسر لا يلزمه الإخراج.
A distinction is made between them, so consideration is given to his poverty at the time of his expiation by fasting. Similarly, a distinction is made in the fidyah of the elderly weak [who cannot fast]: so there is no obligation upon the poor [to pay fidyah], and if he becomes wealthy, he is not obliged to pay it [retroactively].
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage provides a rule regarding kaffarah (expiation) and fidyah (compensation for missed fasts). The principle is that the legal obligation depends on the person's financial ability at the time the obligation becomes due, not at a later time. For kaffarah, if a person is poor at the time he must perform it (e.g., by fasting), then he may fast; later wealth does not require him to give money. Similarly, for the fidyah of an elderly person who cannot fast, if he is poor at the time the fidyah would be due, no payment is required; even if he later becomes wealthy, he is not obligated to make up for it. This illustrates the Hanafi rule that legal responsibility is determined by the state at the time of obligation.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for breaking a fast or oath, etc., which may be by fasting or payment.
فدية (fidyah): Compensation for missed fasts by an elderly person who cannot fast.
إعسار (i'sar): Poverty or inability to pay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what determines whether a person must pay fidyah?
A) His wealth at the time of judgment by a qadi.
B) His ability to fast at the time of obligation.
C) His wealth at the time the fidyah becomes due.
D) The calendar date of Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
The ruling for kaffarah and fidyah is fixed by the person's financial ability at the exact time the obligation becomes due; subsequent changes in wealth have no retroactive effect.

Priority of Debts and Bequests in Estate: A Hanafi Maxim
Hierarchy of estate obligations: a mufti's guide

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hierarchy of obligations in the deceased's estate and apply the maxim that only emancipation and muhabah take priority among bequests.

Core Idea
Debts to Allah drop at death; debts to people bind the estate; among bequests, only emancipation and muhabah take priority.

This passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir lays out a foundational principle for the mufti when determining the order of distribution from an estate. It distinguishes between obligations to Allah, which are forgiven upon death, and obligations to people, which must be satisfied. It also clarifies that among bequests, no preference is given except for emancipation (itq) and preferential treatment (muhabah). Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for issuing correct fatwas regarding inheritance and wills.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two major categories of obligations
Classify obligations into rights of Allah (e.g., zakat, sadaqat al-fitr) and rights of people. Note that the first are dropped at death.
2
Distinguish between secured and unsecured debts
Debts attached to specific property (like a pawn) take priority over debts attached only to the liability (dhimmah).
Secured debts are paid first from the specific property.
3
Analyze bequests for religious obligations
If the will includes obligations like hajj or zakat, the obligatory (fara'id) are given priority, even if delayed. If equal in strength, follow the testator's order.
This applies only if the deceased made a will; otherwise, these obligations are dropped.
4
Apply the general rule for bequests
Among multiple bequests, no priority is given except for emancipation (itq) and preferential treatment (muhabah). The testator's order is not considered unless explicitly stated.
5
Apply the hierarchy to a fatwa scenario
Given a deceased with a secured debt, a will for hajj, and a bequest to a friend, determine the order: secured debt first, then the hajj bequest (if specific), then other bequests equally (unless itq or muhabah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يُقَدَّم على الدين وما يؤخر عنه :
أما حقوق الله تعالى كالزكاة وصدقة الفطر فتسقط بالموت، وإنما الكلام في حقوق العباد فإن وقت التَّرِكَة بالكل فلا كلام وإلا قدَّم المعلّق بالعين كالرهن على ما تعلق بالذمة، وإذا أوصى بحقوق الله تعالى قدمت الفرائض، وإن أخرها كالحج والزكاة والكفَّارات وإن تساوت في القوة بدأ بما بدأ به، وإذا اجتمعت الوصايا لا يقدم البعض على البعض إلا العتق والمحاباة، ولا معتبر بالتقديم والتأخير ما لم ينص عليه. وتمامه في وصايا الزيلعي
What is given priority over debt and what is deferred from it: As for the rights of Allah, such as zakat and sadaqat al-fitr, they are dropped by death. The discussion here is only about the rights of people. If the estate [covers] all [debts], then no discussion; otherwise, what is attached to [specific] property, like a pawn (rahn), is given priority over what is attached to the liability (dhimmah). If one makes a will regarding the rights of Allah, the obligatory (fara'id) are given priority, even if they are delayed, like hajj, zakat, and kaffarat. And if they are equal in strength, he begins with what he began with. If multiple bequests (wasaya) are combined, one does not give priority to one over another except for emancipation (itq) and preferential treatment (muhabah). And no consideration is given to advancing or delaying unless it is stated. Its completion is in the Wasaya of al-Zayla'i.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage discusses the order of priorities in settling the deceased's estate. It differentiates between obligations owed to Allah (such as zakat and sadaqat al-fitr) which are waived by death, and obligations owed to people (debts). When the estate is sufficient for all debts, there is no issue; otherwise, debts secured by specific property (like a mortgage) take precedence over unsecured debts. If the deceased made a will for the performance of religious obligations (like hajj or zakat that were due), these bequests are fulfilled before other bequests, even if they are delayed. Among bequests of equal strength, the testator's own order is followed. As a general rule, no bequest is preferred over another except for freeing slaves and muhabah (selling below market value or gifting). This is a summary; the full details are in the chapter on wills by al-Zayla'i.

Key Terms
دين (dayn): Debt or obligation owed by the deceased.
تركة (tarikah): The estate left by the deceased.
معلق بالعين (muta'allaq bil-'ayn): A debt attached to specific property, like a pawn.
عتق (itq): Emancipation of a slave.
محاباة (muhabah): Preferential treatment in a sale or gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to zakat that was due from the deceased but not paid?
A) It must be paid from the estate first
B) It is dropped and not required
C) It becomes a debt on the heirs
D) It must be paid only if the deceased willed it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule settles estate priorities: Allah's rights drop, secured debts first, then unsecured, and among bequests only emancipation and muhabah take precedence.

Priority for Water Among a Junub, Menstruating Woman, and Deceased
This passage lays out the hierarchy of water entitlement during travel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the priority rules for water distribution among a junub, menstruating woman, and deceased in travel, and explain the legal basis for each case.

Core Idea
Priority for scarce water hinges on the strength of the obligation (fard vs sunnah) and the ability to act as imam.

When traveling, you may encounter a shortage of water needed for purification. Among a junub, a menstruating woman, and a deceased, who gets the water? The Hanafi jurists have detailed rules that depend on ownership of the water and the nature of the obligation. This lesson unpacks those rules from a classic passage in al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three individuals and the common water scarcity
The scenario involves a junub (major impurity), a menstruating woman (also requiring ghusl), and a deceased (requiring washing), with only enough water for one ghusl.
2
Differentiate based on water ownership
The ruling changes depending on whether the water is privately owned (by one or jointly), ownerless (mubah), or given as a gift. List each sub-case from the passage.
Ownership categories: owned by one, jointly owned, mubah, father-son, gift (hibah).
3
Determine the ruling for each sub-case
For each ownership scenario, state who gets priority and the rationale provided in the text (e.g., junub for mubah because his ghusl is fard).
Example: mubah → junub; jointly owned → all do tayammum.
4
Analyze the legal basis: fard vs sunnah and imam capability
The passage contrasts ghusl al-janabah (fard from Quran) with ghusl al-mayyit (sunnah obligation) and notes that a man can lead a woman in prayer, so he gets priority.
This explains why the junub is chosen over the deceased and the woman.
5
Understand the impact of hibah al-musha' on the gift case
The gift case hinges on a rule from Fatawa Qadikhan: a gift of an undivided share in property that can be divided does not transfer ownership, so the deceased cannot accept it.
This is a cross-reference to a madhhab dispute about hibah al-musha'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تذنيب : .
فيما يقدّم عند الاجتماع من غير الديون ثلاثة في السفر: جنب وحائض وميت، وثمة ماء يكفي لأحدهم؛ فإن كان الماء ملكًا لأحدهم فهو أولى به، وإن كان لهم جميعًا لا يصرف لأحدهم ويجوز التيمّم للكل، وإن كان الماء مباحًا كان الجنب أولى به لأن غسله فريضة وغسل الميت سُنّة والرجل يصلح إماما للمرأة فيغتسل الجُنُب وتتيمم المرأة ويُيَمَّم الميت، ولو كان الماء الأب والابن فالأب بین أولى به لأن له حق تملك مال الابن، ولو وهب لهم قدر ما يكفي لأحدهم؛ قالوا الرجل أولى به لأن الميت ليس من أهل قبول الهبة والمرأة لا تصلح لإمامة الرجل. قال مولانا وهذا الجواب إنما يستقيم على قول من يقول إن هبة المشاع فيما يحتمل القسمة لا تقيد الملك وإن اتصل به القبض كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان . ومراده من قوله إن غسل الميت سُنّة ؛ أن وجوبه ،بها بخلاف غسل الجُنُب فإنه من القرآن وينبغي أن يلحق بما إذا كان مُباحًا : إذا أوصى به لأحوج الناس ولا يكفي إلا لأحدهم.
Appendix: On what is given priority when [three things] gather without debts: three [situations] in travel: a person in major impurity (junub), a menstruating woman, and a deceased person. There is water sufficient for only one of them. If the water is the property of one of them, then he is more entitled to it. If it is owned by all of them, it is not to be given to any one of them, and tayammum is permissible for all. If the water is mubah (ownerless), then the junub person is more entitled to it because his washing is a fard (obligatory) while washing the deceased is a sunnah, and the man can be an imam for the woman. So the junub washes, the woman does tayammum, and the deceased is given tayammum. If the water belongs to the father and son, the father is more entitled because he has the right to own the property of his son. If they are given (by hibah) water sufficient for one of them, they said: the man is more entitled because the deceased is not qualified to accept a gift and the woman cannot be imam for the man. Our master (Mawlana) said: This answer is only valid according to the opinion that the gift of undivided property (hibah al-musha') that is capable of division does not transfer ownership even if possession is taken. This is in the Fatawa of Qadikhan. And his meaning when he said that washing the deceased is a sunnah: that its obligation is by sunnah, unlike washing the junub which is from the Quran. And it should be included with the mubah case: if he willed it for the most needy person, and it is not sufficient except for one of them.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This tadhneeb (supplement) deals with a specific scenario in travel where there are three persons: a junub (needing ghusl), a menstruating woman (also needing ghusl), and a deceased person (needing ghusl). Only enough water for one ghusl exists. The ruling varies: If the water is owned by one of them, that person has priority. If jointly owned, none gets it and all perform tayammum. If the water is ownerless (mubah), the junub is given priority because his ghusl is fard from the Quran, while washing the deceased is a sunnah obligation. The woman's ghusl is also obligatory but she can use tayammum. The text then discusses the case where water belongs to a father and son: the father has priority because of his rights over his son's property. When water is given as a gift to all three, the man (junub) is prioritized because the deceased cannot accept gifts and the woman cannot lead prayers for men. The commentator notes that this ruling depends on the view that a gift of undivided common property (musha') that is divisible does not transfer ownership even with possession, as per Qadikhan. The passage clarifies that ghusl of the deceased is sunnah in the sense that its obligation is established by sunnah, not by explicit Quranic text, unlike ghusl for janabah.

Key Terms
هبة المشاع (hibah al-musha'): A gift of an undivided share in common property.
غسل الميت (ghusl al-mayyit): Washing the deceased body.
سنة (sunnah): Here meaning an obligation established by the practice of the Prophet (sunnah), as opposed to Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the travel scenario, if the water is ownerless (mubah), who gets priority?
A) The deceased
B) The junub
C) The menstruating woman
D) All three equally

Key Takeaway
In water scarcity during travel, the person with the stronger obligation (fard from Quran) and the ability to lead prayer gives them priority over sunnah obligations.

The Hanafi Hierarchy of Priorities in Acts of Worship
Rulings on priority between purity and prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of priority (muqaddam) to conflicting acts of worship, identifying which obligation prevails based on time sensitivity and type.

Core Idea
When obligations conflict, the act whose time is most constrained or whose necessity is greater is given priority.

This passage from Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents a series of priority rulings (muqaddamat) that a mufti must know to guide people when multiple obligations coincide. The underlying rule is that the more urgent or essential obligation takes precedence. We will work through the specific cases to extract the governing maxim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first general rule: water for removal of najasah vs hadath
The text states that if a person has both physical impurity (najasah) and ritual impurity (hadath) and only enough water for one, he must use it for najasah.
Because najasah removal is a shart (condition) for the validity of prayer, while hadath can be removed by tayammum.
2
Analyse the second case: funeral prayer vs sunnah prayer
Funeral prayer (fard kifayah) takes priority over sunnah prayers of the time.
The funeral is a communal obligation, so it precedes supererogatory acts.
3
Examine the conflicting scenario of eclipse, Friday, and fard prayer
The text says to prefer the fard prayer if time is tight, except for eclipse because it may be missed due to the eclipse ending.
This introduces the concept of time sensitivity (diyq al-waqt).
4
Handle the combination of Eid, eclipse, and funeral
Funeral is given priority over both Eid and eclipse.
Funeral is a fard kifayah, and it has urgency (death).
5
Note the last ruling: lunar eclipse over witr and tarawih
Lunar eclipse (sunnah muakkadah) takes priority over witr (wajib) and tarawih (sunnah).
Shows that even a sunnah can override a wajib if the sunnah has a narrow window.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما من به نجاسة وهو محدث ووجد ماء يكفي لأحدهما؛ فإنه يجب صرفه إلى النجاسة كما في فتح القدير من الأنجاس. وعلى هذا لو كان مع الثلاثة ذو نجاسة يُقدم عليهم ولم أره . اجتمعت جنازة وسُنَّة وقتية، قدمت الجنازة. وأما إذا اجتمع كسوف وجمعة وفرض وقت لم أره. وينبغي تقديم الفرض إن ضاق الوقت إلا الكسوف لأنه يخشى فواته بالانجلاء، ولو اجتمع عيد وكسوف وجنازة، ينبغي تقديم الجنازة، وكذا لو اجتمعت مع جمعة وفرض ولم يخف خروج وقته، وينبغي أيضًا تقديم الخسوف على الوتر والتراويح.
And as for one who has impurity (najasah) and is in a state of hadath, and finds water sufficient for one of them, then it is obligatory to use it for removing the impurity, as in Fath al-Qadir from 'al-Anjas'. And based on this, if along with the three [the junub, menstruating, deceased] there is someone with impurity, he is given priority over them, but I have not seen [this ruling]. [If] a funeral prayer and a sunnah prayer of the time coincide, the funeral prayer is given priority. And if an eclipse prayer, Friday prayer, and an obligatory prayer of the time coincide, I have not seen [this]. It is appropriate to give priority to the obligatory prayer if the time is tight, except for the eclipse prayer because it is feared that it may pass due to the eclipse ending. And if Eid prayer, eclipse prayer, and funeral prayer coincide, the funeral prayer should be given priority. Similarly, if they coincide with Friday and obligatory prayer and the time is not feared to go out, and also lunar eclipse prayer should be given priority over witr and tarawih.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage provides a hierarchy of priorities in matters of purity and prayers. First, if someone has both ritual impurity (hadath) and physical impurity (najasah) and only enough water to remove one, removing the najasah takes precedence because it is a necessary condition for the validity of prayer. Then the text lists several cases of conflicting obligations: a funeral prayer takes precedence over any sunnah prayer of the time. If an eclipse prayer, Friday prayer, and a fard prayer coincide, the fard prayer is prioritized if time is short, but if time is ample, the eclipse prayer may be done first because it has a narrow window. Funeral prayer is prioritized over Eid and even over Friday when there is no time constraint. Similarly, lunar eclipse prayer takes priority over witr and tarawih.

Key Terms
نجاسة (najasah): Physical impurity on the body or clothing.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity requiring wudu or ghusl.
جنازة (janazah): Funeral prayer.
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse prayer.
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what takes priority if a funeral prayer and a sunnah prayer of the time coincide?
A) The sunnah prayer because it is time-bound
B) The funeral prayer because it is a fard kifayah
C) Both are done together
D) The one that starts first

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes najasah removal over hadath removal when water is insufficient, and funeral prayer over supererogatory acts, while time-sensitivity governs conflicts among obligatory and sunnah prayers.

Choosing Between Virtue and Deficiency: Hanafi Guidance on Conflicting Merits in Worship
Collection of cases where a worshipper must choose between two actions with differing merits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of preferring greater virtue to cases where two actions conflict, and identify the operative ruling for each scenario.

Core Idea
When two virtues conflict, choose the greater reward while avoiding fitna and unnecessary repetition.

This branch from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents classic cases where a worshipper faces a choice: one action has greater merit but a deficiency (like missing congregation), another has less merit but avoids that deficiency. The Hanafi school provides nuanced guidance, often prioritizing congregation, avoiding fitna, and not endorsing repetition of valid prayers for extra virtue. Let's walk through each example and extract the underlying legal maxim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting elements
In each case, determine the two competing actions and their respective virtues or deficiencies (e.g., early time vs. full purity, standing alone vs. congregation).
The text uses terms like 'فضيلة' (virtue) and 'نقيصة' (deficiency).
2
State the Hanafi preference
Find the explicit recommendation in the text: which action does the Hanafi school deem superior?
Look for 'أفضل', 'يستحب', 'ينبغي'.
3
Note conditions and exceptions
Many preferences change based on circumstances like hope of finding water, presence of observers, or ability to perform sunnan.
E.g., 'إن كان طمعا في وجود آخره' for tayammum case.
4
Extract the underlying qa'ida
From these cases, derive the general principle that governs them all.
The qa'ida is not stated but implicit: prioritize greater virtue, avoid fitna, don't repeat valid acts needlessly.
5
Compare opposing views
Note where other schools differ, e.g., the Shafi'i view on praying twice with tayammum then wudu.
This helps solidify the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرع: تقرب من هذه المسائل مسائل اجتماع الفضيلة والنقيصة؛ فمنها الصلاة أول الوقت بالتيمم وآخره بالوضوء ؛ فعندنا يستحبّ التأخير إن كان طمعا في وجود أخره، وإلا فالتقديم أفضل. ولم أر لأصحابنا رحمهم الله أنه يتيمم في أوله ويصلي؛ فإذا وجده آخره توضاً وصلى ثانيًا، ولا يبعد القول بأفضليته وقال الشافعية إنه النهاية في تحصيل الفضيلة. ومنها لو صلّى منفردًا صلى في الوقت المستحب، وإن أخر عنه صلَّى مع الجماعة فالأفضل التأخير ومنها لو كان بحيث لو أسبغ الوضوء تفوته الجماعة ولو اقتصر على مرة أدركها فينبغي تفضيل الاقتصار لإدراكها. ومنها غسل الرجلين أفضل من المسح على الخُفَّين لمَن يرى جوازه وإلا فهو أفضل، وكذا بحضرة من لا يراه. ومنها التوضؤ من الحوض أفضل من النهر بحضرة من لا يراه، وإلا لا . ومنها لو خاف فوت الركعة لو مشى إلى الصف؛ ففي اليتيمة: الأفضل إدراكه في الركوع، وقول النووي في شرح المهذب لم أرَ فيه لأصحابنا ولا لغيرهم شيئًا فقصور، ومنها لو كان بحيث لو صلَّى في بيته صلى قائمًا ولو صلَّى في المسجد لم يقدر عليه؛ ففي الخلاصة : يخرج إلى المسجد ويصلي قاعدًا ومنها لو كان بحيث لو صلى قاعدًا قدر على سُنّة القراءة وإن صلى قائمًا لا قعد وقرأها. ومنها لو ضاق الوقت عن سُنن الطهارة أو الصلاة تركها وجوبًا ولو ضاق الوقت المستحب عن
Branch: Close to these issues are issues of the combination of virtue and deficiency. Among them: prayer at the beginning of time with tayammum and at the end with wudu: According to us, it is recommended to delay if there is hope of finding water at the end; otherwise, early is better. I have not seen from our scholars that he does tayammum at the beginning and prays, then if he finds water at the end, he performs wudu and prays again, and it is not far to say its superiority. The Shafi'is said that it is the ultimate in acquiring virtue. Among them: if one prays alone, he prays in the recommended time, but if he delays and prays in congregation, then delay is better. Among them: if by performing wudu thoroughly he misses the congregation, but by limiting to once he catches it, then limiting is preferable to catch it. Among them: washing the feet is better than wiping over khuffs for one who considers the latter permissible; otherwise wiping is better. Similarly, in the presence of one who does not consider it [permissible]. Among them: performing wudu from a basin is better than from a river in the presence of one who does not consider it permissible; otherwise not. Among them: if one fears missing the rak'ah if he walks to the row, in al-Yatima: it is better to catch it in ruku'. The statement of al-Nawawi in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab 'I have not seen anything from our scholars or others' is deficient. Among them: if by praying at home he can pray standing, but in the mosque he cannot, in al-Khulasa: he should go to the mosque and pray sitting. Among them: if by praying sitting he can perform the sunnah of recitation [properly?], but by praying standing he cannot, he should sit and recite. Among them: if the time is too narrow for the sunnan of purification or prayer, they are left obligatorily. And if the recommended time is too narrow for...
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This branch (far') discusses numerous examples of what to do when two virtuous actions conflict, one having a deficiency. The guiding principle is to choose the action that yields the greater reward or avoids the greater sin. The first example: one can pray at the start of the time with tayammum (due to lack of water) or at the end with wudu. The Hanafi recommendation is to delay if there is hope of finding water; otherwise, pray early. The Shafi'i view is that the best is to pray twice: first with tayammum and then with wudu when found, but this is not our view. Other examples: praying alone in the best time vs. delaying for congregation: congregation is better. If thorough wudu causes missing congregation, minimal wudu is preferred. Washing feet is better than wiping over khuffs except where wiping is not considered valid by the onlooker (to avoid fitna). Similarly, wudu from a basin is better than from a river in presence of objectors. If walking to the row may cause missing the rak'ah, it is better to catch the rak'ah in ruku' by starting from where you are. Praying in the mosque sitting is better than praying at home standing if the mosque provides congregation. If sitting enables proper recitation (sunna) while standing does not, then sit. If time is too short for sunnah actions, they are obligated to be left. The text cuts off in the last example about recommended time being too narrow.

Key Terms
فضيلة (fadilah): Virtue or merit in worship.
نقيصة (naqishah): Deficiency or less merit.
وقت مستحب (waqt mustahabb): Recommended time for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the preferred action if walking to the row may cause missing the rak'ah?
A) Hurry to the row even if it means missing the beginning of the prayer.
B) Catch the rak'ah in ruku' from wherever you are.
C) Wait for the next rak'ah.
D) Signal to the imam to wait.

Key Takeaway
When virtues conflict, Hanafi fiqh prioritizes the greater reward, avoids fitna, and does not encourage repeating valid acts for extra merit.

Preferring Khusuf over Witr and Tarawih
Ruling on preferring khusuf over witr and taraweeh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which the lunar eclipse prayer (khusuf) is given precedence over witr and tarawih, and apply the Hanafi rule of preference for coinciding acts of worship.

Core Idea
Prefer khusuf over witr and tarawih when its time is not feared to exit and it coincides with Jumu'ah and fard.

This lesson examines a specific rule from the Hanafi school regarding the preference of acts of worship when they coincide. The lunar eclipse prayer (khusuf) holds a special status as a sunnah mu'akkadah with a narrow time window. The rule states that when khusuf coincides with Jumu'ah prayer and an obligatory prayer (fard), and there is no fear of its time expiring, it is recommended to give precedence to khusuf over both the wajib witr and the sunnah tarawih. This ruling is based on the principle of precedence for acts with more immediate time constraints.

Guided Path
1
Identify the coinciding acts
The scenario involves the lunar eclipse prayer (khusuf) coinciding with Jumu'ah prayer and another obligatory prayer (fard). Additionally, the rule extends to preferring khusuf over witr and tarawih.
The text specifically mentions 'اجتمعت مع جمعة وفرض'.
2
Check the condition of time
The rule applies only when there is no fear that the time for khusuf will exit (لم يخف خروج وقته). This means the eclipse is still ongoing and there is ample time to perform the prayer.
If the eclipse is ending, the condition fails.
3
Apply the preference rule
Only when the condition is met, give precedence to khusuf over witr and tarawih. The rule is stated as 'وينبغي أيضًا تقديم الخسوف على الوتر والتراويح' meaning 'it is also recommended to give precedence to khusuf.'
This is a recommendation (sunna), not an obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اجتمعت مع جمعة وفرض ولم يخف خروج وقته، وينبغي أيضًا تقديم الخسوف على الوتر والتراويح.
It came together with Jumua and an obligatory prayer, and its time is not feared to exit, and it is also recommended to give precedence to the lunar eclipse prayer over witr and tarawih.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This is a ruling on preferences when acts of worship coincide. The text states: if the lunar eclipse prayer (salat al-khusuf) coincides with Jumua prayer and another obligatory prayer, and there is no fear that its time will expire (i.e., the eclipse is still ongoing), then it is also recommended to give precedence to the lunar eclipse prayer over witr and taraweeh. The wisdom is that the lunar eclipse prayer is a sunnah mu'akkadah with a specific time, whereas witr and taraweeh have broader times. This is a Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms
خسوف (khusuf): The lunar eclipse prayer, a sunnah mu'akkadah.
وتر (witr): The witr prayer, a wajib prayer according to Hanafis.
تراويح (tarawih): The night prayers during Ramadan, sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always, regardless of other prayers.
B) When it coincides with Jumua and another fard, and its time is not feared to exit.
C) Only when it coincides with Jumua.
D) Only if there is fear of time exiting.

Key Takeaway
The lunar eclipse prayer is given precedence over witr and tarawih only when it coincides with Jumu'ah and a fard and there is no fear of its time expiring.

Order of Executing Multiple Hadd Punishments: A Hanafi Rasm al-Mufti Rule
Ruling on order of multiple hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for ordering hudud punishments when multiple converge and identify which punishments take precedence.

Core Idea
When hudud converge, the most severe (death) nullifies the rest; otherwise, order reflects precedence of bodily harm, then honor, then property, then public order.

The Hanafi school provides a detailed order for executing multiple hudud punishments on a single offender, balancing the rights of Allah and individuals. This rule, derived from the principle that a greater hadd prevents the lesser, guides the mufti in cases where multiple crimes have been committed. This lesson parses the rule from al-Muhit as cited in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of hadd punishments mentioned
List the hudud: gouging (for injury), slander (qadhf), theft (sariqa), zina (for non-muhsan: whipping; for muhsan: stoning), drinking (shurb). Also note ta'zir.
2
Understand the general principle
When two hadd converge and it is possible to repel one (i.e., one is death and the other is a lesser punishment), the greater repels the lesser. This is derived from the ability to 'prevent' the lesser.
3
Apply the order for different types (non-muhsan)
The order is: gouging, then slander, then either theft or zina (whipping) at the judge's discretion, then drinking. Drinking is last because it is established by ijtihad.
4
Apply the order for a muhsan offender
For a muhsan: gouging, then slander, then stoning. Stoning is death, which cancels any remaining hadd (like theft or drinking).
5
Consider ta'zir and unresolved cases
Ta'zir precedes hudud because it is a private right (haqq al-'abd). For qisas, apostasy, and zina, qisas takes precedence. For zina and apostasy, stoning takes precedence because it achieves the purpose of both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الحدود إذا اجتمعت ففي المحيط وإذا اجتمع حدان وقدر عى درء أحدهما درىء، وإن كان من أجناس مختلفة، بأن اجتمع حد الزنا والسرقة والشرب والقذف والفقأ بدأ بالفقأ فإذا برىء حدّ للقذف فإذا برىء إن شاء بدأ بالقطع وإن شاء بدأ بحد الزنا، وحدّ الشرب آخرها لثبوته بالاجتهاد من الصحابة رضي الله عنهم، ، وإن كان محصنًا يبدأ بالفقأ ثم بحد القذف ثم بالرجم ويلغي غيرها. (انتهى). ولو اجتمع التعزير والحدود؛ قُدم التعزير على الحدود في الاستيفاء لتمخضه حقا للعبد كذا في الظهيرية، ولم أرَ الآن ما إذا اجتمع قتل القصاص والردة والزنا، وينبغي تقديم القصاص قطعًا لحق العبد، وما إذا اجتمع قتل الزنا والردة، وينبغي تقديم الرجم لأن به يحصل مقصودهما، بخلاف ما إذا قدم قتل الردّة فإنه يفوت الرجم، وإذا قدم قتل القصاص وهو القتل بالسيف حصل مقصود القصاص والرَّدة وإن فات الرجم .
As for hudud when they converge, in al-Muhit: When two hadd penalties coincide and one of them can be prevented, it is prevented. And if they are of different types, such as when hadd of zina, theft, drinking, slander, and gouging converge, one begins with gouging. When he recovers, then hadd for slander. When he recovers, if he wishes he begins with amputation, and if he wishes he begins with hadd of zina. And the hadd of drinking is last because it is established by ijtihad of the Companions. And if he is muhsan, he begins with gouging, then hadd of slander, then stoning, and others are nullified. (End). And if tazir and hudud converge, tazir is given precedence over hudud in execution because it is purely a right of the slave, as stated in al-Zahiriyya. And I have not seen now what if qisas death, apostasy, and zina converge: it should be to give precedence to qisas definitively for the right of the slave. And what if death for zina and apostasy converge: it should be to give precedence to stoning because by it the purpose of both is achieved, unlike if death for apostasy is given precedence because it precludes stoning. And if qisas death is given precedence, which is death by sword, the purpose of qisas and apostasy is achieved even though stoning is missed.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit discusses the order of executing hudud punishments when multiple are due on one person. The general principle is that if one hadd can prevent another (i.e., execution nullifies others), then the preventing one is done first. For different types, the order is: first gouging (for injury), then slander (qadhf), then theft (amputation) or zina (whipping), and finally drinking (shurb). The drinking hadd is last because it was established by ijtihad of the Companions, not definitive text. For a muhsan (married person guilty of zina), the order is gouging, slander, then stoning, and other hadd are cancelled because stoning is death. Tazir (discretionary punishment) is given precedence over hadd because it combines right of Allah and right of slave, but predominantly right of slave. The author adds: for qisas (retaliatory death), apostasy, and zina, qisas should be first because it is a private right. For zina and apostasy, stoning (for muhsan) should be first because it achieves both purposes, whereas killing for apostasy alone would preclude stoning.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Allah for specific crimes.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for crimes not covered by hudud or qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the hadd of drinking placed last in the order?
A) Because it is the least severe.
B) Because it was established by ijtihad of the Companions.
C) Because it involves alcohol, which is less serious.
D) Because it is a right of the slave.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule for executing multiple hudud follows a fixed order: bodily injury, slander, then either theft or zina (non-muhsan) or stoning (muhsan), with drinking last; death penalties cancel all lesser hadd.

The Maxima of Priority (Taqdim) in Competing for Rights
Furuat illustrating the rule of priority (taqdim) with concluding maxim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'No priority without a preponderant factor' to cases of competition in fiqh, and identify the correct murajjih in various furuat.

Core Idea
No one gets priority over another without a valid preponderant factor — precedence or lots decide.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir gathers several cases where priority is given in acts of worship, financial obligations, leadership, marriage compatibility, and judicial procedure. It culminates in a concise maxim that governs all such conflicts: no one is given priority without a preponderating factor (murajjih). As a mufti, you will constantly apply this rule when asked about who should lead prayer, who has the stronger claim, or who gets heard first in a fatwa session.

Guided Path
1
Identify the competition (tazahum)
Determine what right or position is being contested (e.g., leading prayer, debt payment, teaching opportunity).
Competition arises only when multiple parties have claims to the same right.
2
Search for a preponderant factor (murajjih)
Look for an explicit factor that gives one party priority: knowledge, precedence in time, strength of evidence, etc. The passage lists several specific murajjih for different contexts.
The murajjih must be legimitely recognized in the Shariah; not every preference counts.
3
Apply priority if a single murajjih exists
If one party clearly has the superior murajjih, assign priority accordingly (e.g., the most knowledgeable leads prayer).
Sometimes multiple murajjih exist; follow the hierarchical order if given.
4
If no murajjih or equal, resort to lots (iqra')
When all parties are equal in every relevant factor, or no murajjih can be identified, the default is to cast lots. This ensures fairness without bias.
Lots are the last resort, as indicated by the passage's conclusion.
5
Apply the maxim across different furuat
Practice applying the maxim to various real-world scenarios, considering the specific murajjih and possible exceptions.
The passage provides six distinct furuat; use them as templates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استيعاب السنن وينبغي تقديم المؤكدة ثم الصلاة في المستحب، ومنها تقديم الدين المقرّ به في الصحة وما كان معلوم السبب على الدين المقرّ به في المرض. ومنها باب الإمامة ؛ يقدّم الأعلم ثم الأقرأ ثم الأورع ثم الأسنّ ثم الأصبح وجها ثم الأحسن الأحسن زوجة ثم من له جاه ثم الأنظف ثوبًا ثم المقيم على المسافر ثم الحرّ الأصلي على المعتق ثم المتيمم على الحدث على المتيمم عن الجنابة، وتمامه في [خلقا ثم؟] الشرح . ويقرب من هذه المسائل بعض خصال الكفاءة يقابل البعض فالعالم العجمي كفؤ للعربية ولو شريفة وعلمه يقابل نسبها وكذا شرفه . خاتمة : لا يُقدّم أحد في التزاحم على الحقوق إلا بمرجّح ؛ ومنه السبق كالازحام في الدعوى والإفتاء والدرس فإن استووا في المجيء أقرع بينهم.
Comprehensiveness of the sunan: It is better to give priority to the emphasized (sunna mu'akkada), then to prayer in the recommended (mustahab). And among them: giving priority to the debt acknowledged during health and whose cause is known over the debt acknowledged during illness. And among them: the chapter of imamah: the most knowledgeable is given priority, then the most reciter, then the most pious, then the oldest, then the most handsome of face, then the one with the best wife, then the one with status, then the one with the cleanest clothes, then the resident over the traveller, then the freeborn over the freed slave, then the one with tayammum due to hadath over the one with tayammum due to janabah. Its completion is in the commentary. And close to these issues are some qualities of kafa'ah (compatibility) that correspond to each other: the non-Arab scholar is compatible with the Arab woman even if noble, and his knowledge corresponds to her lineage, and similarly his honor. Conclusion: No one is given priority in competition for rights except with a preponderating factor; among them is precedence (as in crowding in a lawsuit, issuing fatwas, and teaching); if they are equal in arrival, lots are cast between them.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (furuat) illustrating the general principle of priority (تقديم) in different chapters of fiqh. It begins with an implicit maxim that in acts of worship, the more emphasized (sunna mu'akkada) takes precedence over the merely recommended (mustahab). Then it moves to financial obligations: a debt acknowledged during health and with a known cause is prioritized over a debt acknowledged during illness (which may be suspect). Next, it lists the criteria for imamah (leading prayer) in order: knowledge, recitation, piety, age, appearance, good spouse, status, cleanliness, residency over travel, free birth over freed slave, and tayammum for minor impurity over major impurity. The text notes that the full details are in the commentary. Then it draws a parallel with kafa'ah (marital compatibility): the non-Arab scholar's knowledge offsets his lineage, making him compatible with a noble Arab woman. The section concludes with a general rule (khātima): no one is given priority in competing for rights unless there is a preponderating factor (murajjih); if all are equal, priority is determined by casting lots. Examples include precedence in lawsuits, issuing fatwas, and teaching. This khātima is itself a minor maxim (dabt) that governs many cases of conflict.

Key Terms
السنن المؤكدة (al-sunan al-mu'akkada): Emphasized sunna acts that are strongly recommended, close to wajib.
الكفاءة (al-kafa'ah): Compatibility between spouses in lineage, religion, profession, and other qualities.
المرجّح (al-murajjih): A preponderating factor that gives one party priority over another in competition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is given priority in leading prayer (imamah) after the most knowledgeable person?
A) The most pious
B) The most reciter
C) The oldest
D) The most handsome

Key Takeaway
Priority in competing for rights is determined by a preponderant factor; when none exists, lots are cast.

Thaman al-Mithl and Valuation Dates in Various Rulings
Listing cases where thaman al-mithl is considered and specifying the valuation date

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct valuation date for each scenario involving thaman al-mithl and apply the qawida across different fiqh chapters.

Core Idea
Thaman al-mithl is the market price; its valuation date shifts by context, and preserving life overrides all normal valuation.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir collects the many places in Hanafi fiqh where the price of the equivalent (thaman al-mithl) is used and specifies the date at which valuation is taken. By studying these furuat, you will understand how a single qawida operates across diverse rulings and how internal differences among the Hanafi imams affect practical outcomes.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida and its scope
Identify the qawida text (القول في ثمن المثل وأجرة المثل ومهر المثل وتوابعها) and note that it covers multiple chapters: tayammum, hajj, sales, ghasb, void contracts, etc.
This qawida is a minor (sughra) one, collecting many related cases.
2
Work through the furuat in order
For each case listed in the passage, identify the fiqh chapter, the ruling, and the specific valuation date (if mentioned) or the principle used.
Pay attention to differences: some cases have consensus, others have ikhtilaf.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on mithli valuation date
For usurped mithli property that becomes unavailable, Abu Hanifa says day of lawsuit, Abu Yusuf says day of usurpation, Muhammad says day of unavailability. Understand the rationale behind each.
The text does not give a tarjih; the mufti must be aware of all positions.
4
Identify the istithna' regarding life preservation
In cases of extreme need (fear of death), thaman al-mithl is not considered; one must buy even at an exorbitant price. This is an exception governed by the maxim 'al-darar yuzal'.
This overrides the normal ruling for tayammum.
5
Consider the practical consequences for a mufti
When issuing a fatwa, the mufti must determine the correct valuation date based on the nature of the property (qimi vs. mithli) and the context (contract, tort, etc.) and must be aware of the internal differences.
Consistency in applying the correct date is crucial for justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القول في ثمن المثل وأجرة المثل ومهر المثل وتوابعها • أما ثمن المثل : فذكروه في مواضع منها : باب التيمّم . قال في الكنز ولو لم يعطه إلا بثمن المثل وله ثمنه لا يتيمم وإلا يتيمم، وفسره في العناية بمثل القيمة في أقرب موضع يعز فيه الماء أو بغبن يسير وفسره الزيلعي بالقيمة في ذلك المكان، لكن لم يبين أنه في وقت عزّته أو في أغلب الأوقات والظاهر الأول، فإن الاعتبار للقيمة حالة التقويم، ويتعين أن لا يعتبر ثمن المثل عند الحاجة لسدّ الرّمق وخوف الهلاك، وربما تصل الشربة إلى دنانير فيجب شراؤها على القادر بأضعاف قيمتها إحياء لنفسه. ومنها : باب الحج ؛ فثمن المثل للزاد والماء القدر اللائق به، وكذا الراحلة كما في فتح القدير. ومنها على قول محمد رحمه الله : إذا اختلف المتبايعان تحالفا وتفاسخا وكان هالكًا فإن البيع يفسخ على قيمة الهالك. وهل تعتبر قيمته يوم التلف أو القبض أو أقلها؟ قال : ومنها إذا وجب الرجوع بنقصان العيب عند تعذر ردّه كيف به؟ قال قاضيخان وطريق معرفة النقصان أن يقوم صحيحًا لا عيب به ويقوم به العيب، فإن كان ذلك العيب ينقص عشر القيمة كان حصة النقصان عشر الثمن. (انتهى). ولم يذكر اعتبارها يوم البيع أو يوم القبض، وكذا لم يذكره الزيلعي وابن الهمام. وينبغي اعتبارها يوم البيع. ومنها المقبوض على سوم الشراء المضمون بتسمية الثمن إذا كان قيميًا ؛ فالاعتبار لقيمته يوم القبض أو يوم التلف قال : ومنها : المغصوب القيمي إذا هلك ؛ فالمعتبر قيمته يوم غصبه اتفاقا . ومنها المغصوب المثلي إذا انقطع قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : تعتبر قيمته يوم الخصومة، وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : يوم الغصب، وقال محمد رحمه الله : يوم الانقطاع . ومنها المتلف بلا غصب تعتبر قيمته يوم التلف ولا خلاف فيه . : ومنها : المقبوض بعقد فاسد تعتبر قيمته يوم القبض لأنه به دخل في ضمانه، وعند محمد رحمه الله تعتبر قيمته يوم التلف لأنه به يتقرر عليه . ذكره الزيلعي في البيع الفاسد . ومنها : العبد المجنى عليه تعتبر قيمته يوم الجناية. ومنها : العبد إذا جنى فأعتقه السيد غير عالم بها وقلنا يضمن الأقل من قيمته ومن أرشه، هل المعتبر يوم الجناية أو قيمته يوم إعتاقه؟ ومنها الرهن إذا هلك بالأقل من قيمته ومن الدين فالمعتبر قيمته يوم الهلاك. لقولهم إن يده يد أمانة فيه حتى كانت نفقته على الراهن في حياته، وكفنه عليه إذا مات، كما ذكره الزيلعي . ومنها: لو أخذ من الأرز والعدس وما أشبه ذلك، وقد كان دفع إليه دينارًا مثلاً لينفق عليه ثم اختصما بعد ذلك في قيمة المأخوذ؛ هل تعتبر قيمته يوم الأخذ أو يوم الخصومة؟ قال في اليتيمة: تعتبر قيمته يوم الأخذ قيل له لو لم يكن دفع إليه شيئًا بل كان يأخذ منه على أن يدفع إليه ثمن ما يجتمع عنده قال يعتبر وقت الأخذ لأنه سوم حين ذكر الثمن. (انتهى). • ومنها ضمان عتق العبد المشترك إذا أعتقه أحدهما وكان موسرا واختار الساكت تضمينه ؛ فالمعتبر القيمة يوم الإعتاق كما اعتبر حاله من اليسار والإعسار فيه كما ذكره الزيلعي .
The discourse on the price of the equivalent (thaman al-mithl), the hire of the equivalent, the dower of the equivalent, and their corollaries. As for thaman al-mithl: they mentioned it in several places, among them: the chapter of tayammum. It is stated in al-Kanz: 'If he is not given [water] except at thaman al-mithl and he has its price, he does not perform tayammum; otherwise he performs tayammum.' Al-Inayah explained it as the equivalent of the value in the nearest place where water is scarce, or with slight overcharging. Al-Zayla'i explained it as the value in that place, but he did not clarify whether it is at its time of scarcity or in most times; the first is apparent. For consideration is the value at the time of appraisal. It is determined that thaman al-mithl is not considered at the need of sustaining life or fear of destruction; sometimes a drink may reach dinars, so it is obligatory for the capable person to buy it at many times its value to save his life. Among them: the chapter of hajj; thaman al-mithl for provisions and water is the amount fitting for him, and similarly the mount, as in Fath al-Qadir. Among them, according to the saying of Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him): When the two parties to a sale differ, they take an oath, rescind the sale, and if the goods are lost, the sale is rescinded based on the value of the lost item. Is its value considered on the day of loss or receipt or the least? He said: Among them, when return for defect becomes obligatory due to inability to return [the sold item], how is it? Qadi Khan said: The method of knowing the defect is to appraise it sound without defect and appraise it with the defect. If that defect reduces one-tenth of the value, then the share of the reduction is one-tenth of the price. (End). He did not mention considering it on the day of sale or receipt, nor did al-Zayla'i and Ibn al-Humann mention it. It should be considered on the day of sale. Among them: goods received on sale contemplation (sum al-shira') that are guaranteed by naming the price, if they are qimi; then consideration is for its value on the day of receipt or loss. He said: Among them: the usurped qimi property when it perishes; its value is considered on the day of usurpation by agreement. Among them: the usurped mithli property when it becomes unavailable [on the market]; Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: its value is considered on the day of the lawsuit; Abu Yusuf said: on the day of usurpation; Muhammad said: on the day of unavailability. Among them: property destroyed without usurpation, its value is considered on the day of destruction, with no disagreement. Among them: goods received under a void contract, its value is considered on the day of receipt because he entered its guarantee by that; according to Muhammad, its value is considered on the day of loss because it becomes established upon him. Al-Zayla'i mentioned it in the void sale. Among them: a slave who is the victim of an injury; his value is considered on the day of the injury. Among them: if a slave commits a crime and the master emancipates him unaware of it, and we say he guarantees the lesser of his value and the compensation; is the consideration on the day of the crime or the day of emancipation? Among them: a mortgage if it perishes, [the liability is] the lesser of its value and the debt; the considered value is on the day of destruction, because they said his hand is a hand of trust over it, so its maintenance is on the mortgagor during his life, and his shroud upon him if he dies, as al-Zayla'i mentioned. Among them: if one takes rice, lentils, and the like, having given a dinar to spend on him, then they dispute about the value of what was taken; is its value considered on the day of taking or the day of lawsuit? Al-Yatimah said: its value is considered on the day of taking. It was said to him: if he had not given him anything, but was taking from him with the intention of paying the price of what accumulates with him? He said: the time of taking is considered because it is a sale contemplation when he mentioned the price. (End). Among them: the guarantee of emancipation of a jointly-owned slave if one partner emancipates him while being wealthy and the silent partner chooses to hold him liable; then the considered value is on the day of emancipation, just as his situation of wealth or poverty is considered therein, as al-Zayla'i mentioned.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive collection of furoo' (applications) revolving around the concept of thaman al-mithl (price of the equivalent) and its valuation dates. It opens by stating the heading, then immediately delves into the first application: the chapter of tayammum. For tayammum, if water is available only at thaman al-mithl and the person can afford it, he must buy it and cannot do tayammum; otherwise he may do tayammum. The scholars explain what thaman al-mithl means: according to al-Inayah, it is the equivalent value in the nearest place where water is scarce, or with slight overcharging; al-Zayla'i defines it as the market value in that locale, but he does not specify whether at the time of scarcity or on average. The passage considers the first interpretation more apparent. It then inserts a critical exception: thaman al-mithl is not considered when there is a genuine fear of death from thirst; in such a case, one must buy water even at many times its value to preserve life. Next it moves to hajj: thaman al-mithl for provisions, water, and mount is the amount befitting the pilgrim's status. Then it addresses the case where two parties to a sale differ as to price or goods, take an oath, and rescind; if the goods are lost, the sale is rescinded based on the value at the time of loss (according to Imam Muhammad). The text then discusses how to calculate compensation for a defect when restitution is impossible, citing Qadi Khan: appraise the item sound and appraise it with the defect; the reduction is proportional. The valuation date for this is recommended to be the day of sale. The passage continues with numerous applications: goods taken on sale contemplation (which are guaranteed by naming a price) – valuation day of receipt or loss; usurped qimi property – valuation day of usurpation by consensus; usurped mithli property when it becomes unavailable – three opinions: Abu Hanifa says day of lawsuit, Abu Yusuf says day of usurpation, Muhammad says day of unavailability; property destroyed without usurpation – day of destruction, no disagreement; goods received under a void contract – day of receipt according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), day of loss according to Muhammad; slave victim of injury – day of injury; slave who commits a crime and is then emancipated without knowledge – whether valuation is day of crime or emancipation; mortgage – day of destruction; taking foodstuffs with a known spending arrangement – day of taking; finally, guarantee of emancipation of a joint slave by the wealthy partner – day of emancipation, considering his financial ability. This collection demonstrates how the general concept of thaman al-mithl is applied across different fiqh chapters, with the valuation date varying based on the nature of the obligation and the school's internal differences.

Key Terms
ثمن المثل (thaman al-mithl): The price of an equivalent, i.e., the fair market value of a commodity in the relevant locality and time.
قيمي (qimi): A type of property that has no standard unit; valuation is based on appraisal.
مثلي (mithli): A type of property that has standard units (like grain); compensation is in kind or value when unavailable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Abu Hanifa's opinion on the valuation date for usurped mithli property that becomes unavailable?
A) Day of usurpation
B) Day of unavailability
C) Day of lawsuit
D) Day of destruction

Key Takeaway
The valuation date for thaman al-mithl varies by legal context; a mufti must know these variations to issue correct rulings.
