The Qawida of Valuation Timing: Applying 'اعتبار القيمة يختلف باختلاف سبب الضمان'
Lists rules for when to assess value in various damage and liability cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'the time of value assessment varies with the cause of liability' to identify the correct valuation date in a given damage or liability scenario.

Core Idea
The valuation date hinges on the cause of liability—consensus for usurpation, day of sale for defects, and ikhtilaf for fungibles.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents a comprehensive list of nineteen legal contexts where the time at which value is assessed determines the compensation amount. The underlying principle is that the valuation date is not arbitrary but tied to the specific cause of liability (sabab al-daman). As a mufti, you must master these distinctions to issue correct fatwas in damage, sale, and tort cases. We will unpack the key categories, the intra-madhhab disputes, and the operative rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause of liability
Determine the legal event that created the obligation to compensate: sale with defect, usurpation, destruction, void contract, tort, etc.
2
Classify the item as qimi or mithli
Non-fungibles (qimi) require individual valuation; fungibles (mithli) can be replaced by similar items, but when unavailable, valuation is needed.
This classification affects whether a dispute arises.
3
Check for consensus or ikhtilaf
Some cases have clear consensus (e.g., usurped qimi valued on day of usurpation). Others have ikhtilaf among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad (e.g., usurped mithli).
The ikhtilaf may change the mufta bihi.
4
Apply the appropriate valuation date
Use the specific date prescribed by the madhhab for that cause. For ikhtilaf cases, apply the mufta bihi position.
The relied-upon position is often Abu Hanifa's.
5
Formulate the fatwa with adab
State the ruling clearly, citing the cause and the valuation date. If applicable, mention the dispute and why the chosen view prevails.
Ensure consistency with other related qawaid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان ذلك العيب ينقص عشر القيمة كان حصة النقصان عشر الثمن. (انتهى). ولم يذكر اعتبارها يوم البيع أو يوم القبض، وكذا لم يذكره الزيلعي وابن الهمام. وينبغي اعتبارها يوم البيع.
ومنها المقبوض على سوم الشراء المضمون بتسمية الثمن إذا كان قيميًا ; فالاعتبار لقيمته يوم القبض أو يوم التلف قال :
ومنها : المغصوب القيمي إذا هلك ; فالمعتبر قيمته يوم غصبه اتفاقا .
ومنها المغصوب المثلي إذا انقطع قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : تعتبر قيمته يوم الخصومة، وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : يوم الغصب، وقال محمد رحمه الله : يوم الانقطاع .
ومنها المتلف بلا غصب تعتبر قيمته يوم التلف ولا خلاف فيه .
ومنها : المقبوض بعقد فاسد تعتبر قيمته يوم القبض لأنه به دخل في ضمانه، وعند محمد رحمه الله تعتبر قيمته يوم التلف لأنه به يتقرر عليه . ذكره الزيلعي في البيع الفاسد .
ومنها : العبد المجنى عليه تعتبر قيمته يوم الجناية.
ومنها : العبد إذا جنى فأعتقه السيد غير عالم بها وقلنا يضمن الأقل من قيمته ومن أرشه، هل المعتبر يوم الجناية أو يوم إعتاقه؟
ومنها الرهن إذا هلك بالأقل من قيمته ومن الدين فالمعتبر قيمته يوم الهلاك . لقولهم إن يده يد أمانة فيه حتى كانت نفقته على الراهن في حياته، وكفنه عليه إذا مات، كما ذكره الزيلعي .
ومنها: لو أخذ من الأرز والعدس وما أشبه ذلك، وقد كان دفع إليه دينارًا مثلاً لينفق عليه ثم اختصما بعد ذلك في قيمة المأخوذ؛ هل تعتبر قيمته يوم الأخذ أو يوم الخصومة؟ قال في اليتيمة: تعتبر قيمته يوم الأخذ قيل له لو لم يكن دفع إليه شيئًا بل كان يأخذ منه على أن يدفع إليه ثمن ما يجتمع عنده قال يعتبر وقت الأخذ لأنه سوم حين ذكر الثمن. (انتهى).
ومنها ضمان عتق العبد المشترك إذا أعتقه أحدهما وكان موسرا واختار الساكت تضمينه ; فالمعتبر القيمة يوم الإعتاق كما اعتبر حاله من اليسار والإعسار فيه كما ذكره الزيلعي .
يعتبر يوم الخصومة القضاء.
ومنها قيمة ولد المغرور الحر، ففي الخلاصة: تعتبر قيمته يوم واقتصر عليه وحكاه في النهاية ثم حكى عن الأسبيجابي أنه والظاهر أن لا خلاف في اعتبار يوم الخصومة. ومن اعتبر يوم القضاء فإنما اعتبره بناء على أن القضاء لا يتراخى عنها. ولهذا ذكر الزيلعي أولاً اعتبار يوم الخصومة، وثانيا القضاء. ولم أرَ مَن اعتبر يوم وضعه .
ومنها: ضمان جنين الأمة قالوا لو كان ذكرًا وجب على الضارب نصف عشر قيمته لو كان حيا، وعشر قيمته لو كان أُنثى ، كذا في الكنز، وفي الخانية. وهما في القدر سواء. وظاهر كلامهم اعتبار يوم الوضع.
ومنها : قيمة الصيد المتلف في الحرم أو الإحرام؛ ففي الكنز في الثاني بتقويم عدلين في مقتله أو أقرب موضع منه ولم يذكر الزمان والظاهر فيهما يوم قتله كما في المتلف .
ومنها : قيمة اللقطة إذا تصدَّق بها أو انتفع بها بعد التعريف ولم يجز مالكها. فالمعتبر فيهما يوم التصدق لقولهم إن سبب الضمان تصرّفه في مال غيره بغير إذنه. ولم أره صريحًا.
ومنها قيمة جارية الابن إذا أحبلها الأب وادعاه. والظاهر من كلامهم الاعتبار بقيمتها قبيل العلوق لقولهم إن الملك يثبت شرطًا للاستيلاد عندنا لا حكمًا.
ومنها : قيمة الصداق إذا انتصف بالطلاق قبل المسيس وكان هالكا، ولم أره صريحًا وينبغي أن يعتبر يوم القضاء به أو التراضي لما قدمناه أنه لا يعود إلى ملك الزوج النصف إلا بأحدهما إذا كان بعد القبض فهذه تسعة عشر موضعا فاغتنمها.
If that defect reduces the value by a tenth, then the share of the deficiency is a tenth of the price. (End). And he did not mention whether it is considered on the day of sale or the day of taking possession, and likewise al-Zayla'i and Ibn al-Humam did not mention it. And it should be considered on the day of sale.
Among them: what is taken on a purchase negotiation, guaranteed by naming the price, if it is a non-fungible; then the consideration is its value on the day of taking possession or the day of destruction, he said:
Among them: the usurped non-fungible if it perishes; its value is considered on the day of usurpation by agreement.
Among them: the usurped fungible if it becomes unavailable; Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: its value is considered on the day of litigation, Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) said: the day of usurpation, and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: the day of cutoff.
Among them: what is destroyed without usurpation – its value is considered on the day of destruction, and there is no dispute about it.
Among them: what is taken under a void contract – its value is considered on the day of taking possession because by it he entered into his liability, and according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) its value is considered on the day of destruction because by it it becomes established upon him. Al-Zayla'i mentioned it in the void sale.
Among them: the slave who is the subject of a tort – his value is considered on the day of the tort.
Among them: the slave who commits a tort and then the master frees him unaware of it, and we say he guarantees the lesser of his value and the damage; is the consideration on the day of the tort or his value on the day of emancipation?
Among them: the pawn if it perishes – [the liability is] the lesser of its value and the debt; so the considered value is on the day of perishing, because, as they said, his hand is a trust hand regarding it, such that its maintenance is on the pawner during his life, and his shroud upon him if he dies, as al-Zayla'i mentioned.
Among them: if one takes rice, lentils and the like, and he had given him a dinar, for example, to spend on it, then they dispute later about the value of what was taken; is its value considered on the day of taking or the day of litigation? He said in al-Yatima: its value is considered on the day of taking. It was said to him: if he had not given him anything, but rather he used to take from him on the basis that he would pay him the price of what accumulates with him? He said: the time of taking is considered because it is a negotiation when the price was mentioned. (End).
Among them: liability for the emancipation of a jointly-owned slave if one of them emancipates him while wealthy and the silent partner chooses to hold him liable; then the considered value is on the day of emancipation, just as his condition of wealth or poverty is considered in it, as al-Zayla'i mentioned.
The day of litigation is considered [for] adjudication.
Among them: the value of the child of a free person deceived. In al-Khulasa: its value is considered on the day of ... and he confined himself to that, and al-Nihaya narrated it, then he narrated from al-Asbijabi that it is apparent that there is no dispute about considering the day of litigation. Whoever considered the day of adjudication only considered it based on the principle that adjudication is not delayed from it. For this reason al-Zayla'i first mentioned considering the day of litigation, and second, adjudication. And I have not seen anyone who considered the day of its birth.
Among them: liability for the fetus of a slave-girl. They said: if it is male, the striker must pay half of one-tenth of its value if it were alive, and one-tenth of its value if it were female, as in al-Kanz and al-Khaniyya. And they are equal in amount. The apparent meaning of their words is consideration of the day of delivery.
Among them: the value of game destroyed in the sanctuary or during ihram. In al-Kanz regarding the second: by evaluation of two just men at its place of killing or the nearest place to it. And he did not mention the time, and the apparent meaning in both is the day of its killing, as in the destroyed [without usurpation].
Among them: the value of a found object if he gives it in charity or benefits from it after announcement and the owner does not approve. The consideration in both is the day of charity, because, as they said, the cause of liability is his disposal of another's property without permission. And I have not seen it explicitly.
Among them: the value of the son's slave-girl if the father impregnates her and claims the child. The apparent meaning from their words is consideration of its value just before conception, because, as they said, ownership is established as a condition for istilad according to us, not as a ruling.
Among them: the value of the dower if it is halved by divorce before consummation and it is perishable. I have not seen it explicitly, and it should be considered on the day of adjudication or mutual agreement because, as we presented, half does not return to the husband's ownership except by one of them if it was after possession. So these are nineteen positions; take advantage of them.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a qawida expansion, listing nineteen distinct legal contexts where the time for assessing value (qimah) is specified. The implicit maxim is: 'The time of valuation depends on the cause of liability.' The author presents each context with the relevant ruling and often a brief rationale or scholarly disagreement. For example, in the case of a defect discovered after sale, value should be assessed on the day of sale (not delivery). In usurpation of a non-fungible, value is on the day of usurpation by consensus; for fungibles, there is ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa says day of litigation, Abu Yusuf says day of usurpation, Muhammad says day of cutoff. The author follows the order of the original work (likely al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir) and cites authorities like al-Zayla'i and Ibn al-Humam. The lesson is a memorization anchor for a mufti to know when to apply which valuation date.

Key Terms
قيمي (qimi): A non-fungible good with no exact substitute; value is assessed individually.
مثلي (mithli): A fungible good that can be replaced by similar items of the same type and quality.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; wrongful possession of another's property without right.
ضعمان (daman): Liability; obligation to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Day of litigation
B) Day of usurpation
C) Day of destruction
D) Day of sale

Key Takeaway
The valuation date for compensation in Hanafi fiqh is determined by the specific cause of liability, with consensus in many cases and intra-madhhab disputes in others that a mufti must know.

When Ujrat al-Mithl Becomes Obligatory: A Dabt Analysis
Dabt listing cases requiring ujrat al-mithl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi cases where ujrat al-mithl is due and apply the governing dabt to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Ujrat al-mithl is due for known craftsmen without a contract or under invalid hire.

This lesson examines a key dabt from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir that lists four scenarios where ujrat al-mithl (fair market wage) becomes obligatory. Understanding this dabt helps muftis determine compensation in ambiguous contracts, invalid agreements, or when a professional works without prior arrangement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dabt and its scope
Recognize that the passage presents a qawida (dabt) listing cases where ujrat al-mithl is wajib. The scope is primarily ijarah and similar transactions.
The dabt is sughra (minor maxim) but covers multiple furu'.
2
Analyze the four cases
Read each case: (1) invalid hire, (2) lessor's threat of extra rent after expiry, (3) buyer saying 'work as before' without wage knowledge, (4) known craftsman working without a contract. Note the exceptions and variations.
In case 2, some say the named amount is due (ikhtilaf).
3
Understand the condition in case 4
The fourth case applies only if the worker is 'known for that craft' (معروف بتلك الصنيعة). If not, ujrat al-mithl is not due.
This is an istithna' (exception) to the general rule.
4
Recognize the mufta bihi position
The text states 'به يفتي' for Muhammad's view in case 4. This is the relied-upon fatwa.
Other views exist but the fatwa is on Muhammad's qawl.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Use the dabt to rule on similar cases: e.g., a freelancer doing work without a contract, or a tenant overstaying after lease ends.
Always verify if the worker is a known professional in that field.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في أُجرة المثل :
تجب في مواضع ; أحدها الإجارة في صور منها الفاسدة، ومنها: لو قال له المؤاجر بعد انقضاء المدة إن فرغتها اليوم وإلا فعليك كل شهر كذا، وقيل يجب المسمى .
ومنها: لو قال مشتري العين للأجير اعمل كما كنت ولم يعلم بالأجر، بخلاف ما إذا علم فإنه يجب.
ومنها : لو عمل له شيئًا ولم يستأجره وكان الصانع معروفًا بتلك الصنيعة وجب أجر المثل على قول محمد رحمه الله وبه يفتي.
Discussion on the like wage (ujrat al-mithl):
It is obligatory in places: one of them is hire in its forms, including the invalid hire, and including: if the lessor says to him after the expiry of the term: 'If you vacate it today, otherwise you owe such-and-such per month,' and it is said the named [wage] is obligatory.
And among them: if the buyer of the property says to the employee: 'Work as you were,' and he is unaware of the wage, contrary to if he knows, then it is obligatory.
And among them: if someone does work for him without hiring him, and the worker is known for that craft, then ujrat al-mithl is obligatory according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) and with this fatwa is given.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a qawida expansion listing cases where ujrat al-mithl (the fair market wage) is due. The first case involves invalid hire contracts; the second is a threat to charge additional rent for delay (some say the named amount is due); the third is when the employer says 'work as before' without specifying wages (if he knows the old wage, that wage is due; if not, ujrat al-mithl). The fourth case is when a known professional works without a contract—according to Imam Muhammad, ujrat al-mithl is due, and this is the relied-upon fatwa. The text uses phrases like 'به يفتي' to indicate the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
أجرة المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for similar work in the same time and place.
الصنعة (al-sin'a): Craft or profession for which the worker is known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No wage is due
B) The named wage if any, otherwise nothing
C) Ujrat al-mithl is due on Muhammad's view and fatwa is given accordingly
D) The worker must negotiate before work

Key Takeaway
Ujrat al-mithl is the default compensation for known professionals who work without a contract or under an invalid hire, ensuring fair pay and preventing exploitation.

Day of Lawsuit or Day of Judgment? The Valuation Day for the Maghrur's Child
First case: valuation day for maghrur's child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the valuation day for the child of a deceived woman (al-maghrur) and explain the Hanafi reasoning for preferring the day of lawsuit over the day of judgment.

Core Idea
Valuation day is tied to the cause of liability, not the act itself.

This passage introduces the first of nineteen cases: the value of the free child of a deceived free woman. Scholars debate whether valuation should be on the day of the lawsuit or the day of judgment. You will learn the Hanafi position and the reasoning behind it, which hinges on the principle that liability arises at the time of the lawsuit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
First, locate the specific case: the value of the free child of a deceived woman (maghrur). Note that the child is free, but compensation is due to the deceived woman from the deceiver.
The maghrur is a free woman deceived into marrying a slave.
2
Locate the Disagreement
The passage notes three possible days: day of birth (placement), day of lawsuit, and day of judgment. Identify which scholars support each view.
Al-Khulasa says day of birth; al-Asbijabi says no disagreement on day of lawsuit.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Tarjih
The Hanafi position, as per al-Zayla'i, prioritizes the day of lawsuit first then the day of judgment. Understand that judgment is considered to follow lawsuit without delay.
The reasoning: liability is fixed at lawsuit; judgment merely enforces it.
4
Extract the Principle
Draw the general rule: valuation day is determined by the moment the cause of liability (sabab) occurs. Here, the lawsuit triggers the liability, not the birth or judgment.
This principle applies across many cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يعتبر يوم الخصومة القضاء. ومنها قيمة ولد المغرور الحر، ففي الخلاصة: تعتبر قيمته يوم واقتصر عليه وحكاه في النهاية ثم حكى عن الأسبيجابي أنه والظاهر أن لا خلاف في اعتبار يوم الخصومة. ومن اعتبر يوم القضاء فإنما اعتبره بناء على أن القضاء لا يتراخى عنها. ولهذا ذكر الزيلعي أولاً اعتبار يوم الخصومة، وثانيا القضاء. ولم أرَ مَن اعتبر يوم وضعه .
اعتبار يوم •
ومنها: ضمان جنين الأمة قالوا لو كان ذكرًا وجب على الضارب نصف عشر قيمته لو كان حيا، وعشر قيمته لو كان أُنثى ، كذا في الكنز، وفي الخانية. وهما في القدر سواء. وظاهر كلامهم اعتبار يوم الوضع.
ومنها : قيمة الصيد المتلف في الحرم أو الإحرام؛ ففي الكنز في الثاني بتقويم عدلين في مقتله أو أقرب موضع منه ولم يذكر الزمان والظاهر فيهما يوم قتله كما في المتلف .
ومنها : قيمة اللقطة إذا تصدَّق بها أو انتفع بها بعد التعريف ولم يجز مالكها. فالمعتبر فيهما يوم التصدق لقولهم إن سبب الضمان تصرّفه في مال غيره بغير إذنه. ولم أره صريحًا.
ومنها قيمة جارية الابن إذا أحبلها الأب وادعاه. والظاهر من كلامهم الاعتبار بقيمتها قبيل العلوق لقولهم إن الملك يثبت شرطًا للاستيلاد عندنا لا حكمًا.
أن
ومنها : قيمة الصداق إذا انتصف بالطلاق قبل المسيس وكان هالكا، ولم أره القضاء به أو التراضي لما قدمناه أنه لا يعود إلى ملك صريحًا وينبغي أن يعتبر يوم الزوج النصف إلا بأحدهما إذا كان بعد القبض فهذه تسعة عشر موضعا فاغتنمها.
The day of the lawsuit is considered (for valuation) and the day of judgment. Among them: the value of the free child of a deceived woman (al-maghrur); in al-Khulasa: its value is considered on the day (of birth) and he confined (the ruling) to it and al-Nihaya reported it, then he related from al-Asbijabi that apparently there is no disagreement in considering the day of the lawsuit. And whoever considered the day of judgment did so based on the fact that judgment does not lag behind it. Hence al-Zayla'i first mentioned considering the day of the lawsuit, then the day of judgment. And I have not seen anyone consider the day of placement.
Consideration of the day •
Among them: the guarantee of the embryo of a slave-girl; they said: if it is male, the striker must pay half of one-tenth of its value if it were alive, and one-tenth of its value if it were female, as in al-Kanz and al-Khaniyya. And they are equal in amount. And the apparent meaning of their statement is considering the day of delivery.
Among them: the value of game destroyed in the Haram or during Ihram; in al-Kanz for the second (case), by valuation of two just witnesses at its place of killing or the nearest place to it, and he did not mention the time, and the apparent meaning in both is the day of its killing, as with destroyed property.
Among them: the value of a found item (luqata) if one gave it in charity or benefited from it after announcement and the owner did not permit it. The considered (day) in both is the day of charity because they said the cause of liability is his disposal of another's property without permission. And I have not seen it explicitly.
Among them: the value of the son's slave-girl if the father impregnates her and claims (the child). The apparent meaning of their statement is consideration of her value just before conception, because they said ownership is established as a condition for istilad (claiming offspring) in our madhhab, not as a ruling.
Among them: the value of the dower if it is halved by divorce before consummation and it is destroyed, and I have not seen (it explicitly) by judgment or mutual consent because we have stated that it does not return to ownership explicitly, and it should be considered on the day (the husband) (took) half, except by one of them if after possession. So these are nineteen places, so take advantage of them.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage enumerates nineteen instances in Hanafi fiqh where valuation is based on a specific day. The author lists them as follows: 1) value of the child of a deceived free woman (maghrur): considered on the day of the lawsuit or judgment, not placement; 2) guarantee of a slave-girl's embryo: value at delivery; 3) value of game destroyed in Haram or Ihram: day of killing; 4) value of a found item: day of charity; 5) value of a slave-girl impregnated by father: just before conception; and others up to nineteen. The author stresses that these are important to remember. The passage is from the Hanafi work Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Ibn Nujaym, focusing on legal maxims and their applications.

Key Terms
الخَصُومَة (al-khusuma): The lawsuit or legal claim; the day when the suit is filed or heard
المَغْرُور (al-maghrur): A deceived party; here specifically a free woman deceived into marriage with a slave

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary valuation day for the child of a deceived free woman (maghrur)?
A) Day of birth
B) Day of lawsuit
C) Day of judgment
D) Day of marriage

Key Takeaway
The valuation day for the maghrur's child is the day of lawsuit, because liability arises from the lawsuit, not the birth or judgment.

intermediate
8 min
Valuation Day in Compensation Cases: Embryo, Game, and Luqata
Three cases of valuation in compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of valuation day to cases of embryo compensation, game destruction, and found items, explaining the reasoning for each.

Core Idea
Valuation day matches the moment the act causing liability occurs.

This lesson continues Ibn Nujaym's enumeration of cases where valuation depends on a specific day. We examine three distinct situations: compensation for harming a slave-girl's embryo, destroying game in the Haram or during Ihram, and disposing of a found item. Each has its own valuation day tied to the causative act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Cases
Locate the three cases in the passage: 1) embryo of a slave-girl, 2) game in Haram/Ihram, 3) found item (luqata). Note the different valuation days mentioned.
Embryo: day of delivery. Game: day of killing. Luqata: day of charity.
2
Analyze the Reasoning for Each
For the embryo, the value is assessed at delivery because until birth, the embryo is not legally a separate entity. For game, the day of killing is used because that is when the harm occurs. For luqata, the day of charity is considered because the liability arises from the finder's disposal (charity) without permission.
In each case, the valuation day is the moment the liability is triggered.
3
Compare with the Maghrur Case
Contrast these cases with the earlier maghrur case: there the liability arose from the lawsuit, not the harm. Here the harm itself is the cause.
The principle: if the act causing damage is direct (killing, disposal), use that day; if liability is through a claim, use the lawsuit day.
4
Extract the Broader Principle
Formulate a generalized rule: valuation day is the day the cause of liability (sabab al-daman) occurs, whether it is an act (killing, disposal) or a legal event (lawsuit).
This principle unifies the various cases.

Source Text

Valuation Day in Family Law: Impregnation and Dower
Two family law cases: istilad and dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the valuation day for a slave-girl impregnated by the father and for a dower halved by divorce, applying the Hanafi principles of istilad and return of property.

Core Idea
Valuation day is shaped by the legal status of ownership, not just the physical event.

This lesson covers two family law cases from Ibn Nujaym's list: a father impregnating his son's slave-girl, and a dower that is destroyed before consummation when divorce halves it. Both involve nuanced ownership rules that determine the moment of valuation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Father-Slave-Girl Case
The father impregnates his son's slave-girl and claims the child. According to Hanafi law, the father owns the child through istilad (ownership of offspring based on ownership of mother at conception). The valuation of the slave-girl is for compensation to the son.
The father must compensate the son for the depreciated value of the slave-girl due to childbirth.
2
Identify the Valuation Day for the Slave-Girl
The passage states: 'الاعتبار بقيمتها قبيل العلوق' – valuation is just before conception. Why? Because ownership for istilad is established as a condition at the moment of conception, not after.
The father's ownership of the child is conditional on his ownership of the mother at conception.
3
Analyze the Dower Case
If a husband gives a dower (mahr) to his wife, then divorces her before consummation, the wife is entitled to half the dower. If the dower item is destroyed, its value must be assessed. The passage says: 'فينبغي أن يعتبر يوم التيقظ' (?) Actually it says 'يعتبر يوم الزوج النصف' – unclear, but the point is that the valuation day is when the title to half is fixed, which is at divorce.
The text is ambiguous; we follow the apparent meaning that valuation is at the day the right to half arises (divorce).
4
Extract the Principle
In both cases, the valuation day is tied to the legal event that creates the entitlement or obligation: conception for the slave-girl, divorce for the dower.
This contrasts with the earlier cases where the causative act (killing, disposal) was the trigger.

Source Text

Instances Where Equivalent Wage (Ujrat al-Mithl) is Obligatory
Listing of applications of a legal maxim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim of ujrat al-mithl by identifying scenarios where it is wajib and distinguishing exceptions based on knowledge, liability, and contract type.

Core Idea
Ujrat al-mithl is due for work/benefit in invalid contracts, usurpation, and fiduciary roles—but not when liability or agreed wage intervenes.

The concept of ujrat al-mithl ensures fair compensation when a contract is flawed or work is done without explicit agreement. In Hanafi fiqh, it is not a universal rule but applies in specific enumerated cases, as listed in this passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. Understanding these cases equips a mufti to correctly determine when a worker is entitled to the market rate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying maxim
Recognize that the passage applies a single principle: ujrat al-mithl is obligatory in specific situations (invalid contracts, usurpation, and fiduciary work).
This is a wusta-level qa'ida governing compensation.
2
Categorize the furuat
Group the scenarios into three categories: invalid contracts (ijarah fasidah, musaqat, muzara'ah, mudarabah), usurpation of benefits (ghasb of orphan/waqf/income property), and fiduciary roles (zakat collector, nazir, wasi, qassam, qadi).
Each category shares the illa of benefit received without valid agreement.
3
Note exceptions and blocking factors
Identify cases where ujrat al-mithl is not due: when wage is known in an invalid contract, when liability (daman) applies (tenant violating condition), when no work is done (zakat collector if owners bring wealth), when judge has not specified wage for nazir, and for wasi of the deceased.
The key blockers are knowledge of wage and existence of daman.
4
Apply the four cautions
Understand the caveats: (1) crop after lease requires court order or consent, (2) known wage in invalid contract binds, (3) payment in currency, (4) wage varies—take average.
These cautions refine the application of the maxim.
5
Synthesize for fatwa
For a given scenario, first check if it belongs to the listed categories, then verify no blocker applies, then apply the cautions to determine the exact amount and modality.
This step builds mufti competence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في أُجرة المثل :
تجب في مواضع ؛ أحدها الإجارة في صور منها الفاسدة، ومنها: لو قال له المؤاجر بعد انقضاء المدة إن فرغتها اليوم وإلا فعليك كل شهر كذا، وقيل يجب المسمى .
ومنها: لو قال مشتري العين للأجير اعمل كما كنت ولم يعلم بالأجر، بخلاف ما إذا علم فإنه يجب.
ومنها : لو عمل له شيئًا ولم يستأجره وكان الصانع معروفًا بتلك الصنيعة وجب أجر المثل على قول محمد رحمه الله وبه يفتي.
ومنها: في غصب المنافع إذا كان المغصوب مال يتيم أو وقفا أو معدا للاستغلال على المفتى به وليس منها ما إذا خالف المستأجر المؤجر إلى شرط بأن حمل أكثر من المشروط فإنه لا يجب أجر ما زاد لأن الضمان والأجر لا يجتمعان . ومنها : إذا فسدت المساقاة والمزارعة كان للعامل أخر مثله .
ومنها : إذا انقضت مدة الإجارة وفي الأرض زرع؛ فإنه يترك بأخر المثل إلى أن يستحصده .
ومنها : إذا فسدت المضاربة فللعامل أخر مثله إلا في مسألة ذكرناها في الفوائد. ومنها : عامل الزكاة يستحق أخر مثل عمله بقدر ما يكفيه ويكفي أعوانه. وفائدته أن المأخوذ أجرة أنه لو لم يعمل ؛ بأن حمل أرباب الأموال أموالهم إلا الإمام، فلا أخر له .
ومنها الناظر على الوقف إذا لم يشترط له الواقف فله أجر مثل عمله حتى لو كان الوقف طاحونة يستغلها الموقف عليهم ؛ فلا أخر له فيها كما في الخانية. وهذا إذا عين القاضي له أجرًا فإن لم يعيّن له وسعى فيه سنة فلا شيء له، كذا في القنية ثم ذكر بعده أنه يستحق وإن لم يشترط له القاضي، ولا يجتمع له أخر النظر والعمالة لو عمل مع العملة. (انتهى).
ومنها : الوصي إذا نصبه القاضي وعيّن له أجرًا بقدر أُجرة مثله جاز. وأما وصي الميت فلا أخر له على الصحيح كما في القنية .
ومنها : القسام لو لم يستأجر بمعين فإنه يستحق أخر المثل. ومنها : يستحق القاضي على كتابة المحاضر والسجلات أجرة مثله.
تنبيهات :
الأول : قولهم في الزرع بعد انقضاء مدة الإجارة يُترك بأجر المثل معناه بالقضاء أو الرضا وإلا فلا أخر له كما في القنية . الثاني : إذا وجب أجر المثل وكان هناك مسمى في عقد فاسد فإن كان معلوما لا يزاد عليه وينقص منه، وإن كان مجهولاً وجب بالغا ما بلغ .
الثالث : يجب أجرة المثل من جنس الدراهم والدنانير .
الرابع : إذا وجب أجرة المثل وكان متفاوتا منهم من يستقصي ومنهم من يتساهل في الأخر يجب الوسط، حتى لو كان أخر المثل اثني عشر عند بعضهم، ٣١٦
Discussion on equivalent wage (ujrat al-mithl):
It is obligatory in places: first, ijarah (hire) in some forms, including the invalid one; and among them: if the lessor says to him after the expiry of the term, 'If you vacate it today, [fine]; otherwise you owe such-and-such each month,' and it is said the named wage is obligatory.
And among them: if the buyer of the property says to the worker, 'Work as you were [doing]' and he did not know the wage; unlike if he knew, then it is obligatory.
And among them: if someone does work for him without hiring him, and the craftsman is known for that craft, then the equivalent wage is obligatory according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), and fatwa is given accordingly.
And among them: in usurpation of benefits, if the usurped property is an orphan's wealth, a waqf, or prepared for exploitation, according to the mufta bihi position; and not included is when the tenant violates the lessor's condition by carrying more than stipulated, for then no wage is due for the excess because liability and wage do not combine.
And among them: if musaqat (sharecropping) and muzara'ah (tenant farming) become invalid, the worker gets his equivalent wage.
And among them: if the term of ijarah expires and there is a crop on the land, it is left with an equivalent wage until it is harvested.
And among them: if mudarabah (partnership) becomes invalid, the worker gets his equivalent wage except in a matter we mentioned in al-Fawa'id.
And among them: the zakat collector deserves an equivalent wage for his work to the extent that suffices him and his assistants. The benefit is that what is taken as wage; if he does not work—by the owners bringing their wealth except the Imam—then no wage for him.
And among them: the supervisor (nazir) of a waqf, if the waqf founder did not stipulate for him, he gets an equivalent wage for his work; even if the waqf is a mill that the beneficiaries use, then he gets no wage therein, as in al-Khaniyya. And this is if the judge specified a wage for him; if he did not specify and he worked for a year, he gets nothing, as in al-Qunyah. Then he mentioned after that that he deserves even if the judge did not specify, and his wage for supervision and work do not combine if he works with the workers. (End).
And among them: the executor (wasi) appointed by the judge, if the judge specified a wage equal to his equivalent wage, it is permissible. But the executor of a deceased gets no wage according to the sound position, as in al-Qunyah.
And among them: the land surveyor (qassam) if he was not hired for a specified amount, he deserves an equivalent wage. And among them: the judge deserves an equivalent wage for writing minutes and records.
Cautions:
First: Their statement regarding the crop after expiry of the ijarah term 'it is left with an equivalent wage' means by court order or mutual consent; otherwise no wage, as in al-Qunyah.
Second: If an equivalent wage is obligatory and there is a named (stipulated) wage in an invalid contract, if it was known, no increase or decrease is made from it; if it was unknown, it becomes due however much it reaches.
Third: The equivalent wage must be in the currency of dirhams and dinars.
Fourth: If an equivalent wage is obligatory and it varies—some being exacting and some being lenient in wage—the average must be taken, even if the equivalent wage is twelve according to some, 316
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage) in Hanafi fiqh, listing numerous situations where it is obligatory. The author begins by noting that it applies in various forms of ijarah (hire), including invalid contracts. Specific cases include: when a lessor imposes a penalty for delay, when a buyer tells a worker to continue without specifying wages, when a known craftsman works without a contract (according to Imam Muhammad—the fatwa position), in usurpation of benefits from orphan property, waqf, or income-generating property (but not when the tenant violates conditions), in invalid sharecropping, when a crop remains after lease expiration, in invalid mudarabah (except one case), for zakat collectors, waqf supervisors, executors appointed by the judge (but not those appointed by the deceased), land surveyors, and judges for clerical work. The passage ends with four important cautions: (1) the ruling on leaving a crop for ujrat al-mithl applies only with court order or mutual consent; (2) if a known wage is stipulated in an invalid contract, it remains binding; if unknown, the market rate applies; (3) ujrat al-mithl must be paid in dirhams and dinars; (4) if wages vary, the average must be taken. This is a typical enumeration of applications of a legal maxim in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
أَجْر المِثْل (ujrat al-mithl): The equivalent wage or market rate for similar work or benefit
الإِجَارَة الفَاسِدَة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): A hire contract that is invalid due to a flaw in conditions or consideration
الضَّمَان (al-daman): Liability to compensate for damage or loss

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a tenant violates a condition (e.g., carries more than agreed), what is the ruling regarding additional wage?
A) He must pay ujrat al-mithl for the excess
B) No wage is due for the excess because liability and wage do not combine
C) He must pay the named wage only
D) He must pay double the wage

Key Takeaway
Ujrat al-mithl is a context-specific compensation tool in Hanafi fiqh, triggered only in particular scenarios and blocked by knowledge of wage or liability.

Cases Where Ajr al-Mithl is Due
Listing cases for ajr al-mithl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scenarios in Hanafi fiqh where ajr al-mithl is due and apply the rule to new cases.

Core Idea
Ajr al-mithl is the default compensation in void contracts and rightful appointments when no valid wage is agreed.

This lesson covers the main cases where the Hanafi school imposes an equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl). From usurpation of benefits to void agricultural contracts, expired leases, and public officials, the principle ensures fair compensation for work performed. Understanding these applications is crucial for fatwa issuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the relationship
Determine whether the scenario involves a contract (e.g., lease, mudaraba) or an appointment (e.g., zakat collector, waqf supervisor).
2
Check validity of contract or appointment
If the contract is valid (sahih), the agreed wage applies; if void (fasid), ajr al-mithl is due. For appointments without stipulated wage, ajr al-mithl may be due.
Exceptions exist, e.g., tenant violating condition, waqf mill case.
3
Apply the rule of Ajr al-Mithl
For each scenario listed, state that ajr al-mithl is due unless a specific exception is mentioned.
The passage lists eight distinct scenarios.
4
Note exceptions and special conditions
In some cases (e.g., usurped property of orphan/waqf, tenant violation, waqf mill), ajr al-mithl is either due or not based on specific conditions.
The tenant violation exception: no wage due for excess because liability and wage do not combine.

Source Text

And among these: In usurpation of benefits, if the usurped property is the wealth of an orphan, a waqf, or prepared for exploitation, according to the fatwa. Not among them is when the tenant violates the lessor's condition by carrying more than stipulated, for then no wage is due for the excess because liability and wage do not combine. And among these: If a musaqah or muzzara'ah contract becomes void, the worker is entitled to an equivalent wage. And among these: If the lease period expires and there is a crop in the land, it is left with an equivalent wage until harvest. And among these: If a mudaraba becomes void, the worker is entitled to an equivalent wage, except for a case we mentioned in the Benefits. And among these: The zakat collector deserves an equivalent wage for his work to the extent that suffices him and his assistants. And among these: The supervisor of a waqf, if the waqif did not stipulate a wage for him, then he has an equivalent wage for his work, even if the waqf is a mill that the beneficiaries operate, then no wage for him therein, as in al-Khaniyya. Then he mentioned after that that he deserves it even if the judge did not stipulate, and the wages of supervision and of work do not combine if he works with the workers. (End). Second: If an equivalent wage is obligatory and there was a named wage in a void contract, then if it is known, it is neither increased nor decreased; if unknown, it is obligatory to the full extent. Third: The equivalent wage must be from the species of dirhams and dinars. Fourth: If an equivalent wage is obligatory and it varies, with some being exacting and some being lenient in the wage, the average must be taken; such that if the equivalent wage is twelve according to some, ten according to some, and eleven according to some, then eleven is obligatory, contrary to valuation: if the valuators differ over a consumed item and two testify its value is ten and two testify less, the higher is taken, mentioned by al-Aqta' in the chapter of theft. Fifth: The equivalent wage in a void lease is pure even if the cause is unlawful. All is taken from al-Quniyya. And we have previously mentioned the ruling on the increase of equivalent wage in the Benefits.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage lists various scenarios where ajr al-mithl (equivalent wage) is due. It begins with cases of usurpation of benefits (ghasb al-manafi), then void sharecropping and farming contracts (musaqah and muzzara'ah), then when lease period expires with crops still in the ground, void mudaraba, then for the zakat collector (amil al-zakat), the supervisor of a waqf, the executor (wasi), the divider (qassam), and the judge (qadi) for writing records. It then provides five admonitions regarding the details of ajr al-mithl, such as conditions for when the wage is due, calculation when there is a named wage in a void contract, the modality in dirhams and dinars, averaging when rates differ, and that the wage in a void lease is pure even if the cause is unlawful. The rulings are from al-Quniyya, a later Hanafi fatwa collection, and the author notes they have previously mentioned the ruling on increase of ajr al-mithl in the section on benefits. All these rules are part of Hanafi methodology for determining compensation and are relied upon for fatwa issuing.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The standard or equivalent compensation for work or benefit, determined by market rate or similar cases.
غصب المنافع (ghasb al-manafi): Usurpation of the benefits of an asset without right, which may obligate compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Void musaqah
B) Expired lease with crop
C) Tenant carrying extra load beyond condition
D) Void mudaraba

Key Takeaway
Ajr al-mithl is the default compensation for work in various void contracts and appointments, with specific exceptions based on the principle that liability and wage do not combine.

Admonitions on Determining Ajr al-Mithl
Admonitions for ajr al-mithl calculation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the five admonitions (tanbihat) for calculating ajr al-mithl in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Ajr al-mithl is calculated by averaging market rates, must be in currency, and is pure income even when the underlying cause is unlawful.

The five admonitions (tanbihat) at the end of the passage provide crucial details for computing ajr al-mithl: when it is actually due, how to treat a named wage in a void contract, the currency requirement, averaging when rates differ, and the purity of the wage despite an unlawful transaction. These rules are essential for issuing precise fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Check if court order or consent exists
Ajr al-mithl is only due if the arrangement is by court order (qada) or mutual consent (rida), otherwise no wage.
This applies to the case of expired lease with crops.
2
Examine existence of a named wage in void contract
If a known wage was named in the void contract, that wage is binding; if unknown, full ajr al-mithl is due.
The named wage is neither increased nor decreased.
3
Specify the currency
Ajr al-mithl must be paid in dirhams or dinars (currency).
This ensures standardisation.
4
Calculate with average when rates differ
If there is variation in market rates, take the average (wasat). For example, if rates are 10, 11, 12, the average is 11.
Contrast with valuation for consumed items where the higher value is taken.
5
Accept purity of wage despite unlawful cause
In a void lease (ijarah fasidah), the ajr al-mithl earned is pure (tayyib) and permissible, even if the contract itself was unlawful.
The wage becomes lawful because the work was performed.

Admonitions: First: Their saying that the crop after the expiry of the lease period is left with an equivalent wage, the meaning is by court order or consent, otherwise he gets no wage, as in al-Quniyya. Second: If an equivalent wage is obligatory and there was a named wage in a void contract, then if it is known, it is neither increased nor decreased; if unknown, it is obligatory to the full extent. Third: The equivalent wage must be from the species of dirhams and dinars. Fourth: If an equivalent wage is obligatory and it varies, with some being exacting and some being lenient in the wage, the average must be taken; such that if the equivalent wage is twelve according to some, ten according to some, and eleven according to some, then eleven is obligatory, contrary to valuation: if the valuators differ over a consumed item and two testify its value is ten and two testify less, the higher is taken, mentioned by al-Aqta' in the chapter of theft. Fifth: The equivalent wage in a void lease is pure even if the cause is unlawful. All is taken from al-Quniyya. And we have previously mentioned the ruling on the increase of equivalent wage in the Benefits.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage lists various scenarios where ajr al-mithl (equivalent wage) is due. It begins with cases of usurpation of benefits (ghasb al-manafi), then void sharecropping and farming contracts (musaqah and muzzara'ah), then when lease period expires with crops still in the ground, void mudaraba, then for the zakat collector (amil al-zakat), the supervisor of a waqf, the executor (wasi), the divider (qassam), and the judge (qadi) for writing records. It then provides five admonitions regarding the details of ajr al-mithl, such as conditions for when the wage is due, calculation when there is a named wage in a void contract, the modality in dirhams and dinars, averaging when rates differ, and that the wage in a void lease is pure even if the cause is unlawful. The rulings are from al-Quniyya, a later Hanafi fatwa collection, and the author notes they have previously mentioned the ruling on increase of ajr al-mithl in the section on benefits. All these rules are part of Hanafi methodology for determining compensation and are relied upon for fatwa issuing.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The standard or equivalent compensation for work or benefit, determined by market rate or similar cases.
الوسط (al-wasat): The average or middle rate when compensation varies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for ajr al-mithl in a void lease where the named wage was unknown?
A) No wage is due
B) Full ajr al-mithl is due
C) The named wage is taken if known, otherwise nothing
D) The average of market rates is taken

Key Takeaway
Ajr al-mithl calculations follow specific rules: known named wages bind, unknown sets full rate, currency required, average taken when rates vary, and the wage is pure even in void leases.

Mahr al-Mithl and Multiplicity of Dower
Explains when mahr al-mithl is obligatory and when multiple dowers are due

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the cases where mahr al-mithl is obligatory and apply the rule of multiplicity of dower to complex family law scenarios.

Core Idea
Mahr al-mithl compensates for consummation; it multiplies in void marriages but not in valid ones.

This passage from al-Ashbah wal-Nadha'ir addresses two interconnected issues: when mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory and whether a single dower multiplies with multiple acts of intercourse. The Hanafi school distinguishes between valid and void marriages, and also considers exceptional cases like joint ownership. Understanding these distinctions is essential for a mufti dealing with complex marriage and dower disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cases where mahr al-mithl is obligatory
List the scenarios: valid marriage without dower, with invalid dower (wine, pig, etc.), with shighar, after consummation or death; void marriage after consummation; shubha intercourse without prior right.
The hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq is the basis.
2
Understand the basis for mahr al-mithl
Recognize that mahr al-mithl is determined by qiyas with women of similar status, focusing on the wife's attributes and custom.
The passage references Sharh al-Kanz for details.
3
Distinguish multiplicity in valid vs void marriage
In valid marriage, Abu Hanifa holds the dower is notionally divisible across acts, so no multiplication. In void marriage, each act triggers a separate mahr.
The exception of a jointly owned slave-girl is noted.
4
Apply the rule to complex cases
The tanbih gives two examples: zina followed by marriage (two dowers) and a conditional divorce formula (multiple dowers). Practice deriving the numbers.
These cases are from Fatawa Qadikhan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند البعض عشرة، وعند البعض أحد عشر، وجب أحد عشر بخلاف التقويم؛ لو اختلف المقوّمون في مستهلك فشهد اثنان أن قيمته عشرة وشهد اثنان أن قيمته أقل الأخذ بالأكثر ذكره الأقطع في باب السرقة. الخامس : أجر المثل في الإجارة الفاسدة يطيب وإن كان السبب حراما .. والكل وجب من القنية. وقدَّمنا حكم زيادة أجر المثل في الفوائد.
الكلام في مهر المثل :
الأصل في اعتباره حديث بروع بنت واشق وبيَّنا في شرح الكنز ما هو وبمن يعتبر، وإنما الكلام هنا في المواضع التي يجب فيها ؛ فيجب في النكاح الصحيح عند عدم التسمية أو تسمية ما لا يصلح مهرًا كالخمر والخنزير والحرّ والقرآن وخدمة زوج حرّ ونكاح آخر. وهو نكاح الشغار ومجهول الجنس والتسمية التي على خطر وفوات ما شرطه لها من المنافع بشرط الدخول في الكل أو الموت. وأما إذا طلقها قبله؛ فالمتعة ولا يتنصف، وفي النكاح الفاسد بعد الدخول، وفي الوطء بشبهة إن لم يقدر الملك سابقا على الوطء ؛ كما في أمة ابنه إذا أحبلها فلا مهر عليه.
بيان ما يتعدد فيه المهر بتعدّد الوطء وما لا يتعدد
أما في النكاح الصحيح؛ فجعله أبو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى منقسمًا على عدد الوطئات تقديرا فلا يتعدد كما لا يتعدد بوطء الأب جارية ابنه إذا لم تحبل وكذا بوطء السيد مكاتبته، وفي النكاح الفاسد، ويتعدد بوطء الابن جارية أبيه أو الزوج جارية امرأته وأفتى والد الصدر الشهيد بالتعدّد في الجارية المشتركة. وتمامه في شرحنا على الكنز .
تنبیه
يجب مهران فيما إذا زنى بامرأة ثم تزوجها وهو مخالط لها؛ مهر المثل بالأول، والمسمى بالعقد ومهران ونصف فيما لو قال : كلما تزوّجتك فأنت طالق فتزوجها في يوم واحد ثلاث مرات ولو زاد بائن ودخل بها في كل مرة؛ فعليه خمسة مهور ونصف. وبيانه في فتاوى قاضيخان .
And according to some it is ten, and according to some it is eleven, so eleven is obligatory contrary to evaluation; if the appraisers differ concerning a destroyed item, and two witness that its value is ten and two witness that it is less, the greater is taken, as mentioned by al-Aqta' in the chapter of theft. Fifth: The like wage in a void hire becomes permissible even if the cause was unlawful... All is from al-Qunyah. We have previously mentioned the ruling on increase of the like wage in the benefits. Discussion on the dower of the like: The basis for considering it is the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq, and we explained in Sharh al-Kanz what it is and by whom it is considered. Here we only discuss the cases where it is obligatory. It is obligatory in a valid marriage when no dower is stipulated or when something unsuitable is stipulated, like wine, pig, a free person, the Qur'an, service of a free husband, and another marriage. It is the marriage of shighar, unknown type, a stipulation that is risky, or loss of the benefits stipulated for her, provided there is consummation in all cases or death. But if he divorces her before that, then there is mut'ah and it is not halved. In a void marriage after consummation, and in intercourse under a shubha if ownership was not previously established over the intercourse, as in the case of his son's slave-girl if he impregnates her, then no dower is due. Clarification of when the dower is multiplied by multiple acts of intercourse and when it is not multiplied: As for a valid marriage, Abu Hanifa made it divisible according to the number of acts of intercourse in estimation, so it is not multiplied, just as it is not multiplied by the father's intercourse with his son's slave-girl if she does not conceive, and likewise by the master's intercourse with his mukatabah. In a void marriage, it is multiplied by the son's intercourse with his father's slave-girl or the husband's intercourse with his wife's slave-girl. And the father of al-Sadr al-Shahid gave a fatwa of multiplication for a jointly owned slave-girl. The complete discussion is in our commentary on al-Kanz. Note: Two dowers are obligatory when a man commits zina with a woman then marries her while still having intercourse with her: the dower of the like for the first, and the stipulated dower for the contract. And two and a half dowers if he says: "Whenever I marry you, you are divorced" and then marries her three times in one day. And if he increases the irrevocable divorce and enters her each time, then five and a half dowers are due. Its explanation is in the Fatawa of Qadikhan.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage begins with a brief ruling on evaluation (taqwim) in cases of destruction: if appraisers differ, the higher value is taken, as cited from al-Aqta' in the chapter of theft. Then it addresses the like wage (ujr al-mithl) in a void hire contract, stating that the wage becomes permissible (halal) even if the underlying cause was haram—this is a well-known Hanafi position distinguishing the contract's invalidity from the right to compensation. The main discussion then turns to mahr al-mithl (dower of the like). The basis is the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq (a Sahaba). Mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory in a valid marriage when no dower is named or when an invalid dower (like wine, pig, etc.) is named, provided there is consummation or death. If divorce occurs before consummation, only mut'ah (consolatory gift) is due, without half. In a void marriage (nikah fasid), mahr al-mithl is due only after consummation. In intercourse under shubha (mistaken belief), it is due only if the man did not previously have the right to intercourse (e.g., a man who impregnates his son's slave-girl owes no mahr because he had a right to her). Next, the text explains multiplicity of dower: In a valid marriage, Abu Hanifa holds that the dower is notionally divisible across acts of intercourse, so it does not multiply by multiple acts (unlike the father's intercourse with his son's slave-girl if no pregnancy). In a void marriage, dower does multiply with each act. A fatwa from the father of al-Sadr al-Shahid (a later Hanafi authority) says it multiplies for a jointly owned slave-girl. The note (tanbih) gives two special cases: (1) If a man commits zina with a woman then marries her while still having intercourse, two dowers are due: mahr al-mithl for the zina (as if it were shubha) and the stipulated dower for the marriage. (2) If a man says 'Whenever I marry you, you are divorced' and marries her three times in one day, three dowers are due if he does not enter; if he enters each time and the divorces are bain, then five and a half dowers are due (three from marriage and two and a half from the divorce-induced remarriages? The text states five and a half). These rulings are drawn from Fatawa Qadikhan. The passage exemplifies how Hanafi jurists derive concrete rules from the foundational hadith and apply them to complex cases.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to what women of similar status receive, determined by factors like family, beauty, wealth, etc.
النكاح الفاسد (al-nikah al-fasid): A marriage contract that is defective due to absence of a condition or presence of a prohibition that does not affect the contract's essence (e.g., marrying without witnesses).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases is mahr al-mithl NOT obligatory according to the passage?
A) Valid marriage with invalid dower (wine) and consummation
B) Valid marriage without dower and death of the husband before consummation
C) Valid marriage with a named dower that is not paid
D) Void marriage after consummation

Key Takeaway
Mahr al-mithl is a default remedy that compensates for consummation, and its multiplication depends on the nature of the relationship—valid or void.

Hanafi Rules on Suspension (Ta'liq) and Conditional Clauses
Defines ta'liq and shart, validity conditions, pillars, lists of contracts, defective conditions, and the maxim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of ta'liq, list the four conditions for its validity, classify contracts as accepting or rejecting suspension, apply the maxim 'Whoever can execute can suspend', and determine the effect of a defective condition.

Core Idea
Ta'liq is valid only in certain contracts; conditions must be possible, connected, and inseparable; the agent for divorce is an exception.

When a person says 'If you enter the house, you are divorced', the divorce is suspended on entry. But not every conditional utterance creates a valid legal effect. Hanafi fiqh lays out precise conditions for a suspension (ta'liq) to be effective. This lesson unpacks those rules, including the conditions, pillars, lists of contracts, the effect of defective conditions, and a key maxim for muftis.

Guided Path
1
Define ta'liq and identify its pillars
Start by stating the definition: linking the occurrence of one sentence's content to another's. Identify the three pillars: a conditional particle, a verb for the condition, and a valid consequence.
If only the particle is present, no suspension occurs.
2
Check the four conditions for a valid ta'liq
Ensure (1) the condition is non-existent but possible, (2) a connector exists if the consequence is deferred, (3) no extraneous separator between condition and consequence, (4) the consequence is a valid legal act. If any condition fails, the suspension is void or becomes immediate.
The fatwa is that if the consequence precedes the condition, the suspension is invalid (immediate effect ruled out).
3
Distinguish contracts that accept suspension from those that do not
Contracts transferring ownership or imposing restrictions cannot be suspended (e.g., sale, hire, gift). Contracts like divorce, manumission, hawala, and surety can be suspended. Memorize the lists in the passage.
If a contract that accepts suspension includes a defective condition, the condition is void but the contract remains valid.
4
Apply the maxim 'Whoever can execute can suspend'
General rule: anyone with authority to perform an act immediately can also suspend it. Exception: the agent for divorce cannot suspend without specific authorization. Conversely, one who cannot execute (e.g., minor) cannot suspend unless tied to ownership.
This maxim provides a quick test for authority to suspend.
5
Determine the effect of a defective condition (shart fasid)
A fasid condition is contrary to the contract's requirements or custom but not impossible. In contracts that accept suspension, the condition is void but the contract stands. In tamlikat (e.g., sale), a fasid condition invalidates the contract. The passage lists 13 contracts invalidated and many that are not.
Use the lists as reference. Tamlikat are invalidated by fasid shart; non-tamlikat are not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القول في الشرط والتعليق
التعليق ربط حصول مضمون جملة بحصول مضمون أخرى. وفسّر الشرط في التلويح بأنه تعليق حصول مضمون جملة بحصول مضمون جملة. (انتهى).
وشرط صحة التعليق ؛ كون الشرط معدومًا على خطر الوجود كالتعليق بكائن
، تنجيز وبالمستحيل باطل ووجود رابط حيث كان الجزاء مؤخرًا وإلا يتنجز، وعدم فاصل أجنبي بين الشرط والجزاء.
ورکنه : أداة شرط وفعله وجزاء صالح فلو اقتصر على الأداة لا يتعلق، واختلفوا في تنجيزه لو قدَّم الجزاء. والفتوى على بطلانه كما بيناه في شرح الكنز . ما يقبل التعليق وما لا يقبله :
تعليق التمليكات والتقييدات بالشرط باطل؛ كالبيع والشراء والإجارة والاستيجار والهبة والصدقة والنكاح والإقرار والإبراء وعزل الوكيل وحجر المأذون والرجعة والتحكيم والكتابة والكفالة بغير الملائم والوقف في رواية والهبة بغير المتعارف، وما جاز تعليقه بالشرط لم يبطل بالشرط الفاسد ؛ كطلاق وعتاق وحوالة وكفالة. ويبطل الشرط، ولا يبطل الرهن والإقالة بالشرط الفاسد وتعليق البيع بكلمة (إن) باطل إلا إذا قال بعت إن رضي أبي.
ووقته كخيار الشرط وبكلمة (على) صحيح إن كان مما يقتضيه العقد أو ملائما له أو جرى العرف به أو ورد الشرع به أو كان لا منفعة فيه لأحدهما. وقد ذكرنا في مدانيات الفوائد ما خرج عن قولهم : لا يصلح تعليق الإبراء بالشرط، وفي البيوع ثلاثين مسألة يجوز تعليقه فيها وجملة ما لا يصح تعليقه .
ويبطل بفاسده ثلاثة عشر : البيع والقسمة والإجارة والرجعة والصلح عن مال والإبراء والحجر وعزل الوكيل في رواية وإيجاب الاعتكاف والمزارعة والمعاملة والإقرار والوقف في رواية .
وما لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد الطلاق والخلع والرهن والقرض والهبة والصدقة والوصاية والوصية والشركة والمضاربة والقضاء والإمارة والكفالة والحوالة والإقالة والغصب والكتابة وأمان القن ودعوة الولد والصلح عن القصاص وجناية غصب وعهد ذمة ووديعة وعارية، إذا ضمنها رجل وشرط فيها كفالة أو حوالة، وتعليق الرد بعيب أو بخيار شرط وعزل قاض والتحكيم عند محمد رحمه الله تعالى، وتمامه في جامع
الفصولين والبزازية.
فائدة :
من ملك التنجيز مَلَكَ التعليق إلا الوكيل بالطلاق؛ يملك التنجيز ولا يملك التعليق . ومَن لا يملك التنجيز لا يملك التعليق، إلا إذا علقه بالملك أو سببه.
Discussion on condition (shart) and suspension (ta'liq). Suspension is linking the occurrence of the content of a sentence to the occurrence of the content of another. Al-Talwih explained the condition as: linking the occurrence of the content of a sentence to the occurrence of the content of a sentence. (End). Conditions for validity of suspension: that the condition is non-existent but possible of existence, like suspension by an existing thing? and [suspension] by the impossible is void, the presence of a connector when the consequence is deferred otherwise it becomes immediate, and the absence of an extraneous separator between the condition and the consequence. Its pillar: a conditional particle, its verb, and a valid consequence. If one restricts to the particle, it is not attached. They differed on its being immediate if the consequence is mentioned first. The fatwa is on its invalidity, as we explained in Sharh al-Kanz. What accepts suspension and what does not: Suspension of transfers and restrictions by condition is void, like sale, purchase, hire, lease, gift, charity, marriage, acknowledgment, release, dismissal of agent, interdiction of the authorized, revocation, arbitration, kitaba, surety without appropriateness, and waqf in one narration, and gift without customary manner. Whatever is permitted to be suspended by condition is not invalidated by a defective condition, like divorce, manumission, hawala, and surety. The condition becomes void but not the contract. The pledge (rahin) and rescission (iqalah) are not invalidated by a defective condition. Suspension of sale with the word 'if' (in) is void unless he says: 'I sold if my father agrees.' Its time is like the option of condition. And with the word 'on' (ala) it is valid if it is something that the contract requires or is suitable for it, or customarily practiced, or stated by the Shariah, or contains no benefit for either party. We have mentioned in Madaniyat al-Fawa'id what is excluded from their statement: 'Suspension of release by condition is not valid', and in sales there are thirty cases where suspension is permitted, and the total of what is not valid. Thirteen things are invalidated by a defective condition: sale, division, hire, revocation, compromise for money, release, interdiction, dismissal of agent in one narration, obligation of i'tikaf, muzara'ah, mu'amalah, acknowledgment, and waqf in one narration. What is not invalidated by a defective condition: divorce, khul', pledge, loan, gift, charity, guardianship, bequest, partnership, mudarabah, judgeship, emirate, surety, hawala, rescission, usurpation, kitaba, protection of a slave, claiming parentage, compromise for qisas, crime of usurpation, covenant of dhimma, deposit, loan (ariyah) if a man stands surety and stipulates in them surety or hawala, suspension of return due to defect or option condition, dismissal of a judge, and arbitration according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him). The complete list is in Jami' al-Fusulayn and al-Bazzaziyyah. Benefit: Whoever has the power to execute (tanjiz) has the power to suspend, except the agent for divorce: he has the power to execute but not to suspend. And whoever does not have the power to execute does not have the power to suspend, unless he suspends it on ownership or its cause.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive Hanafi treatment of shart (condition) and ta'liq (suspension). It opens by defining suspension as linking one clause's fulfillment to another's—essentially a conditional sentence. The condition (shart) is similarly defined. For a suspension to be valid, the condition must be presently non-existent but possible (e.g., 'if it rains'), not impossible (e.g., 'if the dead rise'). Moreover, there must be a connector (rabit) linking the condition and consequence if the consequence is deferred; otherwise the suspension is immediate. No extraneous element should separate them. The pillars of a suspension are three: the conditional word (like 'in' or 'idha'), the verb (the condition itself), and a valid consequence (jaza'). If only the particle is mentioned without a verb, no suspension occurs. The text then notes a dispute: if the consequence is mentioned before the condition, does the suspension become immediate? The relied-upon fatwa is that it is invalid, meaning the suspension fails. The author then lists what can and cannot be suspended. Contracts that transfer ownership or impose restrictions (tamlikat wa taqyidat) cannot be suspended; examples include sale, hire, gift, marriage, acknowledgment, release, etc. On the other hand, divorce, manumission, hawala (transfer of debt), and surety can be suspended. If a contract is validly suspended and a defective condition is added, the condition is void but the contract remains valid (except for some cases like sale and gift which are voided by a defective condition). The text then enumerates thirteen contracts that are invalidated by a defective condition (e.g., sale, hire, waiver of right, i'tikaf) and a longer list of contracts that are not invalidated (e.g., divorce, khul', pledge, loan, gift, etc.). A special rule: a sale suspended with 'in' (if) is void unless the condition is 'if my father agrees' (a condition of approval). A condition expressed with 'ala' (on) is valid if it is appropriate to the contract, customary, or supported by Shariah. A benefit (fa'idah) concludes the discussion: the general rule is that whoever can perform an act immediately (tanjiz) can also suspend it, except an agent for divorce who can divorce immediately but cannot suspend the divorce (because agency is limited). Conversely, one who cannot perform immediately (e.g., a minor) cannot suspend, unless the suspension is tied to ownership or its cause (e.g., a person who will own a slave in the future can suspend manumission on that ownership). This passage is a classic Hanafi resource for muftis to determine the validity of conditional clauses in contracts and other legal acts.

Key Terms
التعليق (al-ta'liq): Linking the occurrence of the content of one sentence to the occurrence of the content of another, i.e., a conditional statement.
الشرط الفاسد (al-shart al-fasid): A condition that is contrary to the contract's requirements or custom, but not totally impossible or unlawful. It renders the condition void but may or may not invalidate the contract depending on the type.
التنجيز (al-tanjiz): Immediate execution of a legal act without suspension.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for the validity of a suspension (ta'liq)?
A) The condition must be impossible
B) There must be a connector between condition and consequence when the consequence is deferred
C) The consequence must be invalid
D) The condition must be mentioned after the consequence

Key Takeaway
A valid ta'liq requires a possible condition, a connector, no separator, and a valid consequence; tamlikat cannot be suspended; and the agent for divorce cannot suspend.

Rulings Related to Travel (Ahkam al-Safar)
Lists the concessions, prohibitions, and conditions associated with traveling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the key rulings of travel (safar) to identify concessions, prohibitions, and conditions, and evaluate the disputed case of a woman's obligation to pay a mahram's expenses.

Core Idea
Travel triggers both concessions (qasr, iftar, mash) and restrictions (woman needs mahram, child needs parental consent, debtor needs creditor permission).

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir presents a comprehensive list of legal effects of travel in the Hanafi school. Travel is not just a physical journey but a legal category that alters many obligations and permissions. Understanding these rulings is essential for issuing fatwas on travel-related matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main concessions of travel
The passage mentions qasr (shortening prayer), iftar (breaking fast during Ramadan), and mash (wiping over socks for three days). Note: these apply only once outside the city limits.
Hanafi concessions begin once one leaves the built-up area of the city, not upon the full three-day journey threshold.
2
List the duties that drop due to travel
Friday prayer, Eid prayers, Udhiya sacrifice, and Takbir al-Tashriq are dropped. Friday prayer is specifically a city obligation.
These are not mere concessions but complete removals of obligation for the traveler.
3
Analyze the restrictions on women travelers
A woman is prohibited from traveling without a husband or mahram, even for Hajj. The presence of a mahram is a condition for Hajj to be obligatory. There is a dispute: if the mahram refuses unless she pays his expenses, is she obliged to pay?
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that she must pay, because the mahram is a condition for performance.
4
Examine restrictions on children and debtors
A child cannot travel without parental consent, except for Hajj if parents are independent. A debtor cannot travel without creditor permission unless the debt is deferred.
These restrictions protect the rights of parents and creditors.
5
Consider special rulings for sea travel
If drowning is feared, Hajj obligation drops. Sea travel may be prohibited. A depositary or executor traveling with deposited property by sea is liable. A cavalryman fighting at sea deserves the cavalry share.
Sea travel has additional risks and thus specific rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القول في أحكام السفر رخصة القصر والفطر والمسح ثلاثة أيام بلياليها وأما التنقل على الدابة فحكم خارج المصر لا السفر . ومنها سقوط الجمعة والعيدين والأضحية وتكبير التشريق. وأما صحة الجمعة فمن أحكام المصر. ومن أحكام السفر حرمته على المرأة بغير زوج أو محرم ولو كان واجبا، ومن ثم كان وجود أحدهما شرطًا لوجوب الحج عليها واختلفوا في وجوب نفقته عليها إذا امتنع المحرم إلا بها والمعتمد الوجوب عليها بناء على أنه شرط وجوب الأداء. ويستثنى من حرمة خروجها إلا بأحدهما هجرتها من دار الحرب إلى دار الإسلام. أحكامه ومن • منع الولد منه إلا برضاء أبويه إلا في الحج إذا استغنيا عنه، وتحريمه على المديون إلا بإذن الدائن، إلا إذا كان مؤجلاً. ويختص ركوب البحر بأحكام : منها سقوط الحج إذا غلبه الهلاك، وتحريم السفر فيه وضمان المودع لو سافر بها في البحر، وكذا الوصي، ويستويان في بقية الأحكام. منها فيما إذا غزا في البحر ومعه فرس فإنه يستحق سهم الفارس كما في الخانية .
Section on the rulings of travel: The concession for shortening prayer, breaking fast, and wiping [socks] for three days with their nights. As for moving on a mount, its ruling is outside the city, not travel. Among its [rulings] is the dropping of Friday prayer, the two Eid prayers, Udhiya, and Takbir al-Tashriq. As for the validity of Friday prayer, it is among the rulings of the city. Among the rulings of travel: its prohibition for a woman without a husband or mahram, even if it is obligatory. Hence, the presence of one of them is a condition for the obligation of Hajj upon her. They differed regarding the obligation of her expenses upon her if the mahram refuses except with it, and the relied-upon is its obligation upon her based on it being a condition for the obligation of performance. An exception from the prohibition of her going out without one of them is her emigration from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam. Among its rulings: prevention of a child from it except with the consent of his parents, except in Hajj if they are independent of him, and its prohibition upon the debtor except with the permission of the creditor, except if it is deferred. Riding the sea has specific rulings: among them is the falling of Hajj if drowning overcomes him, and the prohibition of traveling in it, and the liability of the depositary if he travels with it by sea, and similarly the executor, and they are equal in the rest of the rulings. Among them: if he fights at sea with a horse, he deserves the share of a cavalryman as in al-Khaniyya.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This section from al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir outlines the legal effects of travel (safar) in the Hanafi school. Travel brings about three main concessions: shortening prayer (qasr), breaking fast (fadr) during Ramadan, and wiping over leather socks (mash) for three days and nights. The text notes that moving within the city on a mount is not considered travel; these concessions only apply outside the built-up area. Travel also causes the dropping of Friday prayer, the two Eids, the udhiya sacrifice, and the takbir of tashriq. Friday prayer is valid only in a city (misr). A key ruling is that travel is prohibited for a woman without a husband or mahram, even if the travel is for an obligation like Hajj. This is why the presence of a mahram is a condition for the obligation of Hajj on her. There is a difference of opinion: if a mahram refuses to accompany her unless she pays his expenses, is she obligated to pay? The relied-upon position is yes, because the mahram is a condition for performance. Exceptions to the prohibition of a woman traveling alone include hijra from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam. Additionally, a child cannot travel without parental consent, except for Hajj if the parents are self-sufficient. A debtor cannot travel without the creditor's permission, unless the debt is deferred. Sea travel has its own special rulings: if one fears drowning, Hajj is dropped; sea travel can be prohibited; a depositary and executor are liable if they travel with deposited property by sea. Finally, a soldier on a horse in a sea battle receives the share of a cavalryman.

Key Terms
سفر (safar): Travel beyond the city limits (3 days' journey or more) that triggers legal concessions.
محرم (mahram): A male relative whom a woman cannot marry, e.g., father, brother, son.
رخصة (rukhsa): A legal concession or dispensation that lightens an obligation due to hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling regarding a woman who must pay her mahram's expenses for Hajj because he refuses to accompany her without payment?
A) She is not obliged to pay; she may go alone if safe.
B) She must pay because the mahram is a condition for performance.
C) She must pay only if the mahram is her husband.
D) Hajj becomes obligatory even without a mahram if she pays.

Key Takeaway
Travel legally alters many obligations; a woman's Hajj obligation is contingent on mahram availability, and if she must pay her mahram's expenses, it becomes obligatory.
